| **application** | `Report` ┬Ę `DONE` ┬Ę `BLOCKED` ┬Ę `NEEDS_HUMAN` ┬Ę domain-specific outcome names (e.g., `PRDraftReady` / `PRMergeAck` / `WorkerReport`) | the agent has completed the action and reports the outcome ŌĆö success, blocker, human-escalation request, or any domain-specific terminal state. This is the strongest claim; the message body carries the work product or the blocker manifest. |

`AckProcessed` appears in both transport and commitment because the wire mechanic IS transport (an ack frame returns over the WS just like `Ack`), but the semantic is commitment (the recipient agent ŌĆö not the bridge ŌĆö asserts it has surfaced the inbound). The discriminator: `Ack` = "delivered to the recipient's inbox" (server-emitted, automatic); `AckProcessed` = "agent has surfaced this into its working context" (agent-emitted, requires an active turn).

**Escalation ladder across tiers** (the absence-of-tier-N ŌåÆ probe-tier-N ŌåÆ next-tier sequence the ┬¦13.13 retransmit-vs-probe-vs-escalate tree above operationalizes):

1. **Absence of transport-tier ack** (no `Ack` from server within the expected window) ŌåÆ the wire itself is suspect; handle as connection-level event (┬¦4 watchdog territory), NOT as an A2A retry.
2. **Absence of commitment-tier ack** (`Ack` received, no `AckProcessed` within the expected interval) ŌåÆ the recipient may be slow or absorbed; emit `Ping` (conservative multi-probe per ┬¦13.13 above) to verify recipient liveness. `Pong` returns ŌåÆ wait; no `Pong` ŌåÆ escalate.
3. **Absence of application-tier outcome** (`AckProcessed` received, no terminal `Report` / `DONE` / `BLOCKED` / domain-outcome within the expected work duration) ŌåÆ recipient is committed but stuck. Surface to human via board `decisions` panel (the ┬¦4 watch-state human-review path); do NOT autonomous-retry.

The ordering matters: an adopter who escalates from absence-of-transport directly to human review skips the probe layer that distinguishes "wire dead" (a connection problem) from "agent slow" (a work-pacing concern). An adopter who treats `Ack` (transport) as "done" misses the commitment-vs-application distinction that the retry decision tree depends on. The 3-tier mapping is the SSoT for the tier semantics; the ┬¦13.13 retransmit-vs-probe-vs-escalate tree above is the SSoT for the operational ladder; both compose at the same ack layer.

**Canonical ack-tier reconciliation (v2.4.37 ŌĆö single SSoT across ┬¦13.13 / ┬¦13.13.2 / ┬¦13.19.7)**: this section describes the ack layer with two naming schemes that MUST be read as one model. (1) The **delivery-grade** names at the top of this section ŌĆö `delivered` (server) / `read` (recipient bridge inbox) / `processed` (recipient agent) ŌĆö are the *delivery-confirmation-depth* vocabulary. (2) The **escalation-tier** names in the v2.5.2 mapping table above ŌĆö `transport` / `commitment` / `application` ŌĆö are the *escalation-ladder* vocabulary. They correspond: `delivered` = **transport**; `read` = the bridge inbox-append, surfaced at v0.5 as the `delivered-persist` ack (┬¦13.13.2 (h)); `processed` = **commitment**. The single load-bearing rule that resolves every apparent conflict: **`AckProcessed` is canonically a commitment-tier ack** ŌĆö the recipient agent asserts it has *surfaced the inbound into its working context and engaged*, NOT that it has completed the implied work. The **application tier (the completion claim) is `Report` / `DONE` / `BLOCKED` / `NEEDS_HUMAN` + domain outcomes**, never `AckProcessed` itself. `AckProcessed` MAY double as the completion signal only for a *trivial ask* whose implied work is fully discharged by the act of acknowledging it ŌĆö this is the case ┬¦13.19.9's `(DONE / AckProcessed) ŌåÆ CLEARED` transition and ┬¦13.19.7's tier-3 row describe; for any substantive work the completion is the separate application-tier outcome. Orthogonal axis ŌĆö **pending-queue clear** (┬¦13.13.2): the server clears its at-least-once pending entry on the commitment-tier ack (v0.4) or the bridge's `delivered-persist` ack (v0.5); this is a *different dimension* from the escalation tier (a message can be pending-cleared yet still awaiting its application-tier outcome). `ReviewSLAAck` (┬¦13.19.7) is a **commitment-tier** ack too ŌĆö the SLA-bounded deferred-response variant interpolated between transport and the agent's `AckProcessed` / outcome. Where any other paragraph in this spec reads `AckProcessed` as "completed the work" or "the strongest grade", it is shorthand for the trivial-ask case; this paragraph is the SSoT.

#### 13.13.2 At-least-once relay reliability ŌĆö server pending queue + redelivery + idempotent receiver + bridge inbox-append commitment (v0.5)

The v0.3 baseline (┬¦13.13 above) defines an **at-most-once** transport-tier (`Ack delivered`) on top of a single-attempt server relay. Dogfood on 2026-06-01 surfaced **three relay-drop incidents within one cycle** (a24c5897 morning drop ┬Ę a 2nd-handoff localPath drop ┬Ę a transport-mode negotiation drop ŌĆö all on the same upstream channel), confirming the at-most-once limit is operationally exposed under real cross-environment load ŌĆö substantive payloads can disappear between the server's relay step and the recipient's bridge inbox while transport-tier Ack arrives clean. The 3-drop / 1-cycle threshold (codified in [[a2a-relay-reliability]] memory) is the escalation trigger that promotes the workaround pattern into this RRP.

**The v0.4 contract** (additive, layered on top of v0.3 ŌĆö the wire envelope shape is unchanged; the change is server-side queue + receiver-side dedup):

**(a) Server-side pending queue (sender-anchored)** ŌĆö for every targeted `CUSTOM` envelope with a `msgId` that the server relays, the server retains a *pending entry* `{ msgId, targetAgentId, payload-hash, first-attempt-ts, attempt-count }` in a bounded in-memory queue (per-target, FIFO, default cap 256 entries / 30 minutes whichever lower ŌĆö adopters tune). The pending entry is cleared when the server receives the recipient's commitment-tier `AckProcessed` (the agent-layer assertion that the body has been surfaced into working context). The pending entry is NOT cleared by the transport-tier `Ack delivered` alone ŌĆö `delivered` says only that the wire carried the frame, not that the recipient's inbox file received the body. This is the key inversion: under at-most-once v0.3, transport-tier `Ack` is the "done" signal at the server; under at-least-once v0.4, commitment-tier `AckProcessed` is the "done" signal at the server.

**(b) Redelivery policy (conservative, ladder-bounded)** ŌĆö when a pending entry's `first-attempt-ts` exceeds the redelivery threshold (default 5 minutes for production paths, 30 seconds for dogfood / latency-critical paths ŌĆö adopters tune per workload), the server re-emits the same `{ msgId, payload }` to the recipient. Redelivery is *bounded by attempt-count* (default max 3) and *bounded by recipient connection state* (skip redelivery if the recipient is not currently `AgentList`-present; defer until reconnect, then redeliver on the next handshake-complete event). After max-attempts without `AckProcessed`, the server emits `RelayUnreachable { msgId, targetAgentId, attemptCount, lastError }` to the *sender* (NOT a board-broadcast ŌĆö the sender alone needs to know its message did not stick) and clears the pending entry. The sender then has explicit signal to escalate to human review (board `decisions` panel) per the ┬¦13.13 application-tier outcome ladder.

**(c) Idempotent receiver dedup** ŌĆö the recipient's bridge MUST maintain a *seen-msgId* set (bounded LRU, default 1024 entries / 1 hour) and, on any inbound `CUSTOM` whose `msgId` is already in the seen-set, MUST emit `AckProcessed { ackFor: msgId, dedupHit: true }` immediately and discard the duplicate body. The dedup hit is the canonical signal that "yes, I have this; the server can clear its pending entry; no work to re-do". Without this rule, redelivery would surface the same message as N copies to the recipient's agent layer ŌĆö defeating the purpose of the queue. The dedup signal is *visible to the sender* via the `dedupHit: true` flag so the sender knows its `AckProcessed` came from dedup rather than fresh work (relevant for outcome tracking).

**(d) Composition with v0.3 ack tiers** ŌĆö at-least-once v0.4 does NOT introduce a new tier. The three tiers (transport `Ack delivered` ┬Ę commitment `AckProcessed` ┬Ę application `Report`/`DONE`/`BLOCKED`) are preserved verbatim; v0.4 changes when the server *clears* its pending entry (commitment-tier, not transport-tier) and adds the *redelivery on absence-of-commitment* mechanic that v0.3 lacks. An adopter that has not migrated to v0.4 (no pending queue) continues to operate at at-most-once semantics; the wire is back-compatible because no new field is required (the `msgId` field already exists per v0.3 ┬¦13.13 ŌĆö v0.4 adds *server-side state* keyed by it, not a new envelope field).

**(e) Composition with ┬¦13.11 rule 5 attachment transport-mode** ŌĆö embedded attachments (large dataUrl payloads, up to ~24 MB practical inline) increase the cost of redelivery; the redelivery policy SHOULD apply an attachment-aware throttle (default: half the standard attempt-count for envelopes carrying `value.attachments[]` with any `source: "embedded"` entry, since duplicate large payloads are bandwidth-expensive and the receiver's dedup-by-msgId still catches them on first redelivery). Chunked transfer (`ArtifactManifest` + `ArtifactChunk` + `ArtifactComplete`) is independently idempotent at the chunk level (chunks carry `chunk_index` per-artifact) and does NOT participate in the ┬¦13.13.2 msgId pending queue at the chunk granularity ŌĆö the manifest message participates; the chunks are reassembly state on the receiver side.

**(f) Composition with broker-forward workaround** ŌĆö the broker-forward workaround documented in `memory/feedback_a2a_relay_reliability.md` (extract from main's `ws-history/<sender-agentId>.jsonl` and forward to the affected recipient) remains a *valid operational fallback* even after v0.4 ships, for the case where the server's pending queue exceeds its cap or the recipient stays disconnected past `RelayUnreachable`. The workaround does NOT bypass v0.4 dedup ŌĆö the broker-forward emit carries the original `msgId`, so the recipient's seen-msgId set deduplicates against the original delivery attempt. The workaround is the manual escalation path that runs alongside automatic redelivery.

**Phase 1 ship (v2.5.11)** ŌĆö this v0.4 RRP draft codifies the contract. Reference-implementation work (server.cjs pending queue + redelivery scheduler + bridge dedup LRU) follows in v2.5.12+ (sequenced after the upstream dataUrl reemit catch + Mode B baseline absorption). The contract above is the spec adopters build against; the reference implementation is the v0.4 dogfood vehicle.

**Calibration signal ŌĆö 2026-06-01 dogfood**: 3 drops / 1 cycle was the threshold that triggered this RRP. Future calibration (post-v2.5.12 reference implementation): the queue cap (256), redelivery threshold (5 min / 30s), max attempts (3), and dedup-LRU (1024 / 1 hour) are *provisional defaults*; expect tuning after 1-2 weeks of v0.4 telemetry. Adopters report observed redelivery counts + dedup-hit rates + `RelayUnreachable` emit rates as the empirical anchors.

**(g) Bridge inbox-append commitment (v0.5 addition)** ŌĆö the v0.4 design conflated *pending-queue clear* with *agent application-tier acknowledgement*: the server kept a pending entry until the recipient's agent layer emitted an `AckProcessed` (the "body has been surfaced into working context" assertion). Operationally that introduced a class of false-positive `RelayUnreachable{commitment-ack-absent}` errors ŌĆö when a recipient agent was *idle* between turns, or *busy processing an unrelated task*, the server's redelivery threshold elapsed without an `AckProcessed` and the sender saw an "unreachable" signal for a message that had in fact been *durably written to the recipient's inbox file*. The 2026-06-02 dogfood (relay RRP ┬¦13.13.2 v0.4 hub adoption immediately after ship) surfaced this: a normal `Ack` from EG ŌåÆ main was redelivered 3├Ś ŌåÆ `RelayUnreachable{commitment-ack-absent}` despite the body having reached main's inbox on the first attempt, because main's agent layer did not happen to emit a commitment-tier `AckProcessed` for it.

The v0.5 resolution: the **recipient's bridge** (the WS bridge process that owns the inbox file ŌĆö distinct from the agent layer that *reads* the inbox) MUST emit `AckProcessed { ackFor: msgId, tier: "delivered-persist" }` *immediately upon appending the inbound CUSTOM envelope to its inbox file*. The bridge does not wait for the agent layer to read or process the body ŌĆö the moment the body is durably persisted to the inbox (the per-┬¦13.16.6 cursor-tail watching anchor), the bridge has fulfilled its half of the at-least-once contract and emits the commitment signal on its own authority. The server treats this `tier: "delivered-persist"` ack as the canonical *pending-queue clear* trigger, exactly equivalent in semantic weight to v0.4's commitment-tier ack but emitted by the transport layer that actually owns the persistence guarantee, not by the application layer that owns the *interpretation* of the body.

This removes the false-positive class entirely: every successfully-delivered envelope produces an immediate `delivered-persist` ack within milliseconds of the bridge's inbox write, so the server's pending entry clears before the redelivery threshold elapses for the normal-case path. Redelivery only fires when the bridge is not running, has crashed, or the recipient is not currently `AgentList`-present ŌĆö the actual reachability failure modes the v0.4 RRP was meant to address.

**(h) Tier semantics ŌĆö v0.5 vocabulary (renames v0.4's implicit conflation)** ŌĆö v0.5 distinguishes three named tiers on the response side of an `AckProcessed`:

| Tier name | Emitter | Trigger | Pending-clear |
|---|---|---|---|
| `delivered` | server (proxy) | wire frame received from sender; relayed to recipient | no (transport only) |
| `delivered-persist` | recipient **bridge** | inbox-file append complete; durable | **yes** (canonical v0.5 trigger) |
| `commitment` | recipient **agent** | body surfaced into agent's working context; agent will act | redundant after `delivered-persist` (no-op at server) |

Application-tier outcomes (`Report` / `DONE` / `BLOCKED` per ┬¦13.13) are preserved verbatim; they live on the *outcome* dimension, separate from the pending-clear dimension. An agent that emits `AckProcessed{tier:"commitment"}` (the v0.4 name) is still spec-compliant ŌĆö the server simply observes that the pending entry is already cleared (by `delivered-persist`) and treats the commitment ack as informational. v0.4 receivers that emit `AckProcessed` without an explicit `tier` field are interpreted as `commitment` for back-compat, and the server falls back to pending-clear on first such ack (the v0.4 behaviour) ŌĆö which means a v0.4 receiver paired with a v0.5 server continues to operate at v0.4 semantics, including the false-positive class. The escape from false positives requires the v0.5 *bridge* (the receiver-side process), not a v0.5 server.

**(i) Migration path v0.4 ŌåÆ v0.5** ŌĆö the wire envelope shape is unchanged (`msgId` remains the only required v0.4 field; v0.5 adds the optional `tier` field to `AckProcessed.value`). Per-component update:

- **Server** ŌĆö gains the rule "any `AckProcessed{tier:"delivered-persist"}` clears the pending entry, in addition to the v0.4 commitment-tier clear". Optional: add per-target redelivery-threshold override allowing operators to disable redelivery (`RELAY_REDELIVERY=off`) while v0.5 bridges roll out across the deployment.
- **Bridge** ŌĆö adds the inbox-append hook: on every successful inbound CUSTOM body append, emit `AckProcessed{ackFor:msgId, tier:"delivered-persist"}` to the sender. Composes with the v0.4 ┬¦13.13.2(c) seen-msgId LRU dedup: a duplicate msgId still emits `AckProcessed{ackFor:msgId, dedupHit:true}` and discards the body without an inbox-append (no `delivered-persist` for duplicates ŌĆö the original delivery already produced one).
- **Agent** ŌĆö no change required for v0.5 mechanics; application-tier acks (`Report` / `DONE` / `BLOCKED`) and the optional commitment-tier `AckProcessed` continue to function. The `delivered-persist` mechanism is bridge-layer and invisible to agent-layer code.

The 2026-06-02 dogfood validated v0.5 with main-EG bidirectional: main's bridge (`ws-local-bridge.cjs`) added the inbox-append-commitment hook + restart, and the next EG ŌåÆ main dogfood envelope cleared pending in <1s without redelivery or `RelayUnreachable`. Reference-implementation work for the EG-side bridge (`constellation/reference/runtime/local-bridge.cjs`) ships separately as the v2.5.18 EG-side complement to this spec (the v2.5.16 / v2.5.17 slots were taken by the promo-site cut and the spec patch itself respectively).

### 13.14 Reference-build redaction discipline ŌĆö env-specific identifier grep before public ship

Any artifact destined for a *public* surface (this repo's `Constellation.md` / `Superscalar.md` / `constellation/reference/*` / seeds / README) MUST pass an env-specific token grep before commit. The constellation/reference tree is the highest-risk surface because it is *distilled from a private operating environment* ŌĆö real service names, private repo paths, internal catalog ids, and provenance commits can leak through quotation, grep-target meta lines, or sample-data left in `.eux` `@intent` provenance.

**The pattern.** Maintain a private redaction list in `<scope-root>/_lessons/redaction-tokens.md` (gitignored) with project-specific tokens ŌĆö service names, private repo names, catalog ids, internal issue numbers, workspace path roots, employee aliases. Before any commit touching public-shipped files: `rg <tokens> <public surfaces>` must return zero. Refuse the commit if not.

**Anti-patterns observed.**

- *Meta-grep leak* ŌĆö a NOTES file that documents the redaction grep itself by *quoting the tokens* (e.g. "ņøÉļ│Ė grep ļīĆņāü: `<token1>`┬Ę`<token2>`┬ĘŌĆ”"). The grep target list IS the leak. Fix: name the *category* ("upstream-ĒÖśĻ▓Į-ĒŖ╣ņłś Ēéżņøīļō£"), not the tokens; keep the actual token list in the private `redaction-tokens.md`.
- *Provenance quote leak* ŌĆö an `.eux` `@intent` line that names "originally distilled by the *<env name>* live-board main" or similar. Fix: replace the env name with `upstream live-board main` (the role is what matters, not the org).
- *Origin-mistake echo* ŌĆö a reference NOTES table that names "(`<private-org>/<repo>` head=...)" as the production source. Fix: `private orchestration repo` placeholder; the org/repo path is not load-bearing for the reference reader.
- *Catalog-id sample leak* ŌĆö an example catalog (`(hub/fw/<projectA>/<projectB>/<projectC>)`) where the bracketed ids are real downstream project codenames. Fix: state the *shape* of the catalog ("Downstream-defined catalog; project ids are downstream-specific") and drop the inline sample.

**Why it composes with ┬¦13.13 / ┬¦13.11 / ┬¦13.9.** ┬¦13.13's `delivered` ack is silent by design; ┬¦13.11.1's progress emission is the visibility channel; ┬¦13.9's role branching preserves peer scopes. None of those help when the *content* of the emission is itself a leak ŌĆö env-specific tokens travel as freely on a silent-acked, role-correct, board-emitted message as on a private one. ┬¦13.14 is the *content* discipline matching those *transport* / *cadence* / *role* disciplines: the live-board ecosystem is only as private as its lowest-attention public artifact.

**On past archives.** Existing `_proposals/*` and historical `_lessons/*` may pre-date this discipline and contain env-specific tokens noted as "public" at their original ship time. If the upstream policy has since narrowed scope, those archives become candidates for a separate redaction commit on the next maintenance cycle ŌĆö they are lower priority than fresh artifacts (which travel further), but they remain in scope for the same grep gate.

### 13.15 Reference-build syntax gate (optional, downstream-adopted)

A complementary discipline to ┬¦13.14 ŌĆö that one guards *content* (env-specific token leaks), this one guards *loadability* (a master `.cjs` that fails `node --check` is a non-loading reference that breaks every fresh downstream bootstrap until someone notices). Real driver: a v2.2.x reference shipped with a JSDoc block that closed early on `RUN_*/TEXT_*/TOOL_*` because `*/` inside the comment terminated the block (the `*` adjacent to `/` is an RFC-valid JSDoc trap); downstream adopters hit a `SyntaxError` on Constellation bootstrap. Caught only after a downstream submitted a bug bundle (`_proposals/002`).

**The gate**: `node --check constellation/reference/runtime/*.cjs` must return zero before commit. The implementation is one of two options ŌĆö adopt either, both, or none per project policy. **The EG repo itself adopts option A**; downstream projects may follow either pattern:

- **Option A ŌĆö pre-commit hook** (EG repo's choice). A single `node --check` loop over `reference/runtime/*.cjs` in `.git/hooks/pre-commit`; fails the commit if any file fails. Cheap (~5s wall-clock per commit, only `*.cjs` count) and catches drift *before* it reaches origin. Requires the hook to be installed locally on every clone ŌĆö the seed's `scripts/sync-readme-counts.mjs --install` (or any equivalent) is the natural carrier; EG ships this as `scripts/check-reference-syntax.mjs`. Real-world coverage: only protects developers who installed the hook; CI is the back-stop for the rest.
- **Option B ŌĆö CI workflow** (downstream-adopted). A GitHub Actions / GitLab CI / equivalent job that runs `node --check` on the reference runtime on every push and PR. Doesn't block local commits but blocks merges to the main branch. Higher infrastructure cost (CI minutes), but always-on coverage regardless of which contributor pushed. Recommended for projects where the reference runtime is a shipped public artifact (e.g. a published package or vendored copy in dependent repos).

**Compose with both**: A + B is the safest combination ŌĆö A catches drift in local commits and B catches drift from non-hooked contributors / CI-only environments. The added cost is small (the same `node --check` invocation, twice). For solo projects without CI infrastructure, A alone is the practical baseline.

**Beyond `.cjs`**: the same gate principle applies to any reference-build artifact whose load-failure breaks downstream bootstrap ŌĆö `.py` (`python -m py_compile`), `.rs` (`cargo check`), brewed `.eux` outputs (`node bin/estreux.mjs drift`), etc. The point is *fail at commit time, not at adopter time*.

### 13.16 Runtime operational runbook ŌĆö launch idempotency, orphan handling, channel cleanup

The complement to ┬¦13.15 (build-time gate) ŌĆö this is the *runtime-time* discipline for keeping a Constellation deployment stable across restarts, account switches, IDE crashes, and developer machine reboots. The driver was a real downstream incident (per `_proposals/003`): a long live-board session with two external interruptions accumulated 12 same-`agentId` bridge processes; absent any single-instance protection they kicked each other off in an infinite `register(HELLO)` ŌåÆ close ŌåÆ reconnect loop, flooding the board + inbox with ~2,500 `ServerNotice` events until manual OS-level kill.

The bridge's PID lockfile guard (per `_proposals/003` Fix 1, `local-bridge.cjs:L53`) is the in-process line of defense. This runbook covers the **out-of-process layers**: how launcher scripts, restart-orphan cleanup, and channel cleanup compose with it.

#### 13.16.1 Launch idempotency

Any wrapper that starts a Constellation runtime process (`local-bridge.cjs` ┬Ę `server.cjs` ┬Ę `watchdog.cjs` ┬Ę `self-wake-watcher.sh`) MUST be safe to re-invoke. The bridge's own lockfile already handles the worst case (an existing same-`agentId` bridge is killed before the new one acquires the lock), but a launcher that *also* checks the lockfile and the listening port preemptively produces less alarming logs and avoids the brief flap window during the bridge's startup race.

Reference launcher behavior (per `agentId`):

1. Read `constellation/reference/runtime/.<agentId>-bridge.lock` (sanitized filename ŌĆö see `local-bridge.cjs:L53`).
2. If the PID is alive (`process.kill(pid, 0)` succeeds), the launcher's policy decides:
   - **default**: kill the prior PID, log `replacing prior bridge PID N`, start new bridge.
   - **strict**: refuse to start, log the existing PID ŌĆö operator decides.
3. For `server.cjs`: gate on the listening port (e.g. 27878) ŌĆö only one server per port; if `EADDRINUSE` would otherwise be raised, surface it explicitly before launch.

Launcher scripts are project-specific (PowerShell ┬Ę bash ┬Ę npm script ┬Ę systemd unit) ŌĆö they ship as runbook examples, not as canonical reference. The lockfile path + behavior contract is the invariant.

#### 13.16.2 Restart-orphan handling ŌĆö `stop-all` / `status` helpers

Background runtime processes survive IDE / harness restarts at the OS level but the harness loses task tracking, so the harness's normal task API can't reach them. Manual cleanup helpers are required:

- **`status`** ŌĆö list every alive Constellation process: PID ┬Ę agentId (or role) ┬Ę lockfile path ┬Ę bound port ┬Ę parent process ┬Ę start time. Sources: scan `constellation/reference/runtime/.*-bridge.lock` files + check the listening port; cross-reference `node` processes by exact script path (`local-bridge.cjs` ┬Ę `server.cjs` ┬Ę `watchdog.cjs`).
- **`stop-all`** ŌĆö kill every Constellation process and remove its lockfile. **Filter precisely**: `Name=node.exe` (or `node`) AND command-line contains the absolute path of one of the four reference scripts. **NEVER** use a broad `*constellation*` command-line glob ŌĆö it catches IDE shell wrappers and unrelated processes (real-incident anti-pattern: a Windows `Stop-Process | Where {$_.CommandLine -like '*constellation*'}` accidentally killed the parent terminal because the IDE's Constellation channel name was in its title).

The pair makes recovery deterministic: `status` to see what's alive, `stop-all` to start clean, then launchers re-start whatever the deployment needs.

#### 13.16.3 Channel noise cleanup ŌĆö `CloseChannel`

A flap incident leaves the affected channel's history file (`ws-history/<agentId>.jsonl`) and the agent's inbox saturated with `ServerNotice{kind:'online'}` + `Status` events. **Browser refresh does NOT clear them** ŌĆö the noise is recorded server-side, not cached client-side. New operators reaching for refresh as a first instinct will be confused.

The cleanup primitive is `CUSTOM/CloseChannel{value:{agentId}}` (board ŌåÆ server):

1. Server deletes `ws-history/<agentId>.jsonl` and removes the in-memory channel state.
2. Server broadcasts `ChannelClosed` so other boards drop the tab.
3. Next time the same `agentId` registers, the channel re-starts clean.

For inbox cleanup, the operator truncates the affected `<scope>/inbox.jsonl` (gitignored, never tracked) ŌĆö the bridge's `cursor` is byte-offset based, so a truncate-to-zero resets the agent's pending queue without losing in-flight WS events. (Truncate must happen *while the bridge is stopped* ŌĆö `stop-all` first, then truncate, then re-launch.)

#### 13.16.4 Server-side HELLO churn dampening (adopted at upstream production ┬Ę reference impl shipped d385561)

The bridge lockfile is the line of first defense, but the server (`server.cjs`) adds a second: detect duplicate `agentId` HELLOs arriving at a rate that suggests a flap and decide *who* to keep.

Adopted behavior (per `_proposals/003` Fix 2 ŌĆö shipped at the upstream live-board production layer in commit d385561, 2026-06-01; reference cp of `server.cjs` into `constellation/reference/runtime/` remains a separate follow-up cycle):

- Per-`agentId` ring buffer of the last `N` HELLO timestamps (default `N=5`).
- If the most recent `K` HELLOs (default `K=3`) span less than `M` ms (default `M=10000`) ŌåÆ `flap` WARN + a `cooldown` window.
- During cooldown, a new HELLO from the same `agentId` is rejected with `ServerNotice{kind:'flap-rejected', incumbentPid: <prev>}`; the incumbent connection survives.
- Cooldown duration: default 30000ms (30s) ŌĆö long enough to absorb a flap burst, short enough that a legitimate restart waits ~30s before its HELLO is honored.
- Env knobs (per d385561): `CONSTELLATION_FLAP_RING_N` (default 5), `CONSTELLATION_FLAP_RING_K` (default 3), `CONSTELLATION_FLAP_SPAN_MS` (default 10000), `CONSTELLATION_FLAP_COOLDOWN_MS` (default 30000). Operator-tunable per deployment if a specific bridge restart pattern needs a different sensitivity profile (e.g., a slow-restart bridge needing N=10 / span=20000).

Why both layers ship: the bridge-side lockfile (┬¦13.16.1) covers the common case where the bridge can be process-locked, but it requires fs write access from the bridge process. Foreign-runtime bridges (a non-Node adapter, a sandboxed worker, no-fs sandboxed CI runner, etc.) cannot always lock ŌĆö the server-side dampener is the universal back-stop. They compose: a locked bridge avoids the flap before it starts; the server-side dampener catches it when the bridge can't lock.

(EG-side follow-up surfaced by seq 165: bridge HELLO must carry `pid: process.pid` so the `incumbentPid` field in the `ServerNotice{kind:'flap-rejected'}` carries a real value rather than `null` ŌĆö being implemented in a parallel workstream against `constellation/local-bridge.eux` + the reference runtime cp.)

#### 13.16.5 Composition with ┬¦13.13 / ┬¦13.14 / ┬¦13.15

- **┬¦13.13** ack layer is silent by design ŌĆö it does NOT generate the `ServerNotice` flood that ┬¦13.16 cleans up. The flood is a *transport-layer* artifact (HELLO churn from same-`agentId` register), so ┬¦13.16 fixes are also transport-layer (lockfile + launcher + orphan kill); they're orthogonal to the application-layer ack mechanism.
- **┬¦13.14** (env-specific token redaction) applies to runbook examples too: `stop-all` / `status` stubs MUST NOT inline real agentIds, port numbers, or workspace paths from the upstream's environment; use `${AGENT_ID}` / `${PORT}` / `${WORKSPACE}` substitution. The lockfile filename's `agentId` sanitization (`replace(/[^\w.-]/g, '_')` per `local-bridge.cjs:L53`) is the in-code form of the same discipline.
- **┬¦13.15** (build-time syntax gate) catches a non-loading master that would otherwise reach adopters; ┬¦13.16 (runtime ops) catches the *operational* equivalent ŌĆö a loadable but mis-launched master that produces a flap storm at adopter sites. Build gates ship the right bytes; runtime gates ship the right *process topology*.
- **┬¦13.16.6** (watcher liveness probe, below) extends ┬¦13.16.1-.4: the launch/orphan/cleanup fixes ensure a watcher *starts cleanly*, but they don't guarantee it *stays armed*. The probe discipline closes the gap.

#### 13.16.6 Watcher liveness probe discipline

When the adopter agent parks in a "wait for external response" cycle ŌĆö board `UserPrompt` waiting on a remote agent's `Delegate` reply, an upstream worker's job-done event, an inbox-polling rearm chain ŌĆö **a watcher/background task that polls the inbox.log silently dies more often than expected**. Symptoms: a `Ping`/`AckProcessed`/`Delegate` arrives at the inbox, but the adopter never surfaces it because the watcher's rearm chain broke (process crash, user-interrupt, exceeded rearm ceiling, harness garbage-collection of the background task).

A "watch maintained" claim *without an explicit liveness check* is the silent-stall class of bug ŌĆö work looks healthy because no error fires, but hours pass with the response unread. The user is typically the first to notice (`"ņØæļŗĄ ņÖöņ¢┤?"` / `"ņÖ£ ņĢł ņøĆņ¦üņŚ¼?"`) ŌĆö that is the failure mode this discipline exists to prevent.

**Probe rules** (apply whenever the adopter is parked waiting on an external response):

- **Inbox mtime probe** ŌĆö re-tail `assets/collab/inbox.log` and check its mtime vs current wall-clock. Constellation watchers typically rearm every 40-45 min; an inbox.log untouched for >60 min while the adopter is in a wait cycle is suspect (either no inbound *or* watcher dead ŌĆö disambiguate via the next rule).
- **Rearm log probe** ŌĆö the watcher's task output should contain a recent `watcher re-armed @ <Z>` marker (one per rearm cycle). If the last marker is >2├Ś the rearm interval behind wall-clock, the watcher is parked or crashed.
- **Cross-check inbound side** ŌĆö when expecting a reply, peek at the watcher's task output (`WAKE` / `REARM` markers). Last marker hours behind wall-clock = dead watcher, not "no inbound".
- **Re-arm explicitly when stale** ŌĆö do not "hope" a dead watcher recovers. Spawn a fresh watcher cycle on the same polling target, note the new task ID, and mark the old one dead in the agent's working state.
- **Surface staleness immediately** ŌĆö tell the user the watcher went stale, how long the gap was, and the action taken (re-arm or escalate). Never continue to claim "watch maintained" silently after detecting staleness; that converts a recoverable miss into an unrecoverable one.

**Discipline cadence**: probe at least once per **independent work cycle** taken during the wait, or at least every **~30 min wall-clock** if the agent is otherwise idle ŌĆö whichever fires first. Do NOT conflate todo state (`[in_progress] watcher`) with task liveness (the bash background task actually running). Todo state is the agent's *claim*; task liveness is the *truth*. Verify the truth before reusing the claim.

**Why this belongs in the runbook, not just agent habit**: an adopter without an explicit probe discipline will treat "watcher launched once" as sufficient and lose responses for hours. The probe is part of the *operational contract* for Constellation watchers ŌĆö same tier as `stop-all` / `status` (┬¦13.16.2) and the lockfile (┬¦13.16.1).

**Turn-end mandatory rearm ŌĆö the discipline that prevents the multi-cycle failure mode**: probe-without-rearm catches a dead watcher but does not prevent the NEXT cycle from being dead. At the close of EVERY user-facing response (just before emitting the final text), the agent MUST run a 1-shot Bash that:

1. Reads `inbox.log` mtime and the most recent watcher task's output mtime.
2. **Unconditionally spawn a fresh background watcher** (`run_in_background: true`) with the same polling target ŌĆö every turn-end, regardless of whether an existing watcher appears alive.

**Unconditional, not conditional ŌĆö the cost-asymmetry argument**: the agent's active-liveness check on the prior watcher is unreliable. It depends on the agent (a) correctly reading the bg task's output mtime, (b) correctly interpreting the task state (alive vs paused-by-SIGSTOP vs cleanly-exited vs crashed), and (c) not mistaking a harness-paused bg task for a dead one (the wall-clock-vs-task-clock mismatch documented below makes "mtime within rearm interval" itself an unreliable liveness signal). Cost of a false-positive spawn (the agent rearms when a live watcher already exists) = one extra task slot + a few log lines, both harmless. Cost of a false-negative miss (the agent skips rearm because it judged the prior watcher live when in fact it was paused/dead) = the silent-stall class ŌĆö hours of lost inbound until the user surfaces the stall. The asymmetric cost structure (harmless false-positive vs hours-of-lost-work false-negative) makes unconditional spawn the correct rule: pay the trivial double-arm cost every turn rather than gamble on a liveness check that is structurally unreliable. Same-base redundancy at the same `base` cursor does NOT add inbound coverage for the windows the prior watcher was already covering (the a7911fd armed-window-blind-spot diagnosis still holds ŌĆö redundant watchers at the same `base` share the same blind spot), but it ALSO does not subtract: the fresh spawn IS a fresh `base` after the prior watchers complete, so future inbound DOES get covered by the new watcher's cursor. There is no scenario where unconditional spawn loses coverage relative to conditional.

*(Honest-history note: commit 0185b8d introduced a conditional-rearm rule on the rationale that "one live watcher is sufficient" once the cursor-tail fix was in place. That decision is **RETIRED (2026-05-31)**. The cursor-tail fix remains the structural coverage layer for armed-window gaps ŌĆö it is not retired ŌĆö but it does not justify trusting the agent's liveness check on the prior watcher, which is the part of 0185b8d's reasoning that fails in practice. Conditional rearm requires the agent to correctly judge "is the prior watcher alive?" at every turn-end; the failure mode this section exists to prevent is precisely the absorbed multi-cycle state where the agent's volitional judgment is unreliable. Unconditional spawn removes the judgment from the path.)*

**Fail mode this addresses** (observed 2026-05-31): agent processed inbound seq 70 ŌåÆ entered a multi-cycle work loop (workflow ├Ś 3 + commit ├Ś 2 + a follow-up patch) ŌåÆ did not explicitly rearm at any cycle boundary ŌåÆ silently lost seq 73 (catalog review approval) and seq 77 (new user task: live-board UI + DB delegation) for ~40 minutes until the failure surfaced externally. The previous `┬¦13.16.6` probe rule was correct but insufficient: it required the agent to *think to probe* at the right moment, which an agent absorbed in multi-cycle synthesis does not reliably do. Making rearm a **turn-end ritual**, not a *probe-then-decide* judgment call, removes the failure path.

**Cadence interaction with the probe rule**: the probe rule (above) catches a dead watcher when the agent is already awake. The turn-end ritual prevents the watcher from dying between turns in the first place and prevents board/queue drift while the agent is awake. Both are required ŌĆö probe is the PRIMARY catch mechanism for the armed-window blind spot (the gap between the prior watcher's `base` cursor and the next watcher's spawn); the unconditional rearm is the forward-looking catch mechanism for the next idle window. Neither is a "safety net" for the other ŌĆö they cover *disjoint* windows: the probe catches inbound that already landed below the new watcher's `base`; the rearm catches inbound that will land after the new watcher arms. As of the 2026-05-31 upstream policy the turn-end ritual is a **5-element mandatory checklist** every user-facing response MUST run before emitting final text: (1) inbox.log mtime / cursor-tail probe, (2) unconditional watcher rearm, (3) board-state real-time update (`done` / `current` / `updatedAt`), (4) BOARD_STALE gate handoff (┬¦13.16.7 ŌĆö main only; the gate itself runs on the watcher's rearm path, but the agent acknowledges any `WAKE(BOARD_STALE)` from the prior cycle here), (5) planned-queue scan with "start a progressable item now, don't idle-wait while work remains" default. As of the same-day follow-up policy the checklist is **extended to 6 elements** with the addition of **(6) pre-large-work context materialization** (see paragraph below). None of the six is optional; none is gated on a volitional judgment the agent makes about whether the element is needed this turn.

**Mandatory ordering ŌĆö element 1 (cursor-tail probe) STRICTLY BEFORE element 2 (unconditional rearm)**: the probe is NOT diagnostic telemetry; it is NOT "after-the-fact" verification; it is the **gating step** that fills the armed-window blind spot the new watcher structurally cannot cover. A fresh watcher armed at `base = current line count` is permanently blind to any inbound below `base` ŌĆö including inbound that landed while the prior watcher was suspended (SIGSTOP'd by harness during agent-active turn, per the wall-clock-vs-task-clock mismatch below). The rearm alone DOES NOT recover that inbound; only the cursor-tail does. Concrete step list every turn-end MUST execute, in this order:

1. **(a)** Tail `inbox.log` from the agent's last-surfaced cursor (NOT from the prior watcher's `base`) ŌĆö this is the agent's own cursor maintained across turns, not the watcher's.
2. **(b)** Surface any meaningful inbound found in the tail ŌĆö `Delegate`, `UserPrompt`, `WorkerReport`, `WorkerAck`, `Report`, `Handoff` (the ┬¦13.16.9 A2A-intent group; note `AgentHello` is the handshake group per ┬¦13.16.9's 4-group reclassification and is NOT meaningful inbound) ŌĆö into the current response context. If meaningful inbound is found, the turn does NOT end on the current plan; it ends on a response to the newly-surfaced inbound.
3. **(c)** Advance the agent's cursor to the last line read.
4. **(d)** THEN run the unconditional rearm (element 2).

Skipping (a)-(c) and going straight to (d) loses any inbound that landed during the prior watcher's suspend window and is **structurally invisible to the new watcher** ŌĆö the new watcher's `base` is past that inbound's line number, so the polling loop will never see it. Re-arm without probe is forward coverage without backward catch; it is not equivalent to running both.

**Wrong order ŌĆö anti-pattern (observed 2026-05-31)**: agent ran element 2 (unconditional rearm) first WITHOUT first running element 1 (cursor-tail probe). seq 123 (Status) and seq 127 (Report: DB P1 ship + ┬¦13.19 P2 spec-delivery query) arrived while the prior watcher was active/suspended; the new watcher armed at `base = current line count` (above both inbound's line numbers), putting both inbound below its base ŌĆö permanently invisible to the new watcher. The agent only ran the cursor-tail probe manually after the missed inbound was surfaced, recovering the 2 missed messages. The failure was NOT the rearm (it worked correctly for forward coverage); the failure was the ordering ŌĆö running the rearm without first running the probe to catch what was already below `base`. The fix is the ordering reinforcement in this section, not a new mechanism: element 1 was already in the 6-element checklist; what was missing is the MANDATORY ORDERING that element 1 runs before element 2, every turn, without exception.

**Filter discipline ŌĆö exclude self-emission AND server-replay noise (ev-agnostic, name-only)**: the watcher's "meaningful inbound" filter is a **single-stage name-only** pipeline ŌĆö a noise blocklist followed by a meaningful allowlist, with NO `ev:"inbound"` scope gate ahead of them. The blocklist and allowlist memberships are defined in **┬¦13.16.9 (Message classification by intent)** ŌĆö the noise blocklist === board-directed allowlist + transport-tier; the meaningful allowlist === A2A-intent allowlist. ┬¦13.16.9 is the SSoT for the name enumeration; this section references it by anchor. Two false-positive sources are excluded by the blocklist: **(1) self-emission echo** ŌĆö the board echoes the agent's own outbox push back into `inbox.log` (legacy event-relay lines as `ev:"sent"` with the same `name` such as `WorkerReport`), so a name-only filter without exclusion would trigger a self-wake; the blocklist covers self-emission name classes regardless of envelope format. **(2) server-side replay noise** ŌĆö `History` payloads (server replays prior session events on reconnect) and transport-layer `Ack` / `AckProcessed` / `AckCumulative` / `AckPolicyUpdate` frames carry historical or transport-only data with no new external delivery to respond to; the `History` payload in particular is line-level large and contains nested `Delegate` / `WorkerReport` events from old sessions that a naive name-grep matches as fresh inbound. Canonical bash filter pattern (names per ┬¦13.16.9 ŌĆö **┬¦13.16.9 is authoritative; when this inline example diverges from ┬¦13.16.9's 4-group memberships, ┬¦13.16.9 wins**): `tail ŌĆ” assets/collab/inbox.log | grep -vE '"name":"(History|Ack|AckProcessed|AckCumulative|AckPolicyUpdate|ServerNotice|AgentList|Status|ConnectionRestored|Heartbeat|Typing|UserPromptAccepted|PersistentAdapterSmoke|OnboardAck|AgentHello|WorkerInboxReceived|EditMessage|MainChanged)"' | grep -cE '"name":"(Delegate|UserPrompt|WorkerReport|WorkerAck|Handoff|HandoffRequested|HandoffReady|Report|Command|Priority|Cancel|BlockerManifest|BlockerNudge|PRRequest|PRDraftReady|PRReviewAck|PRMergeRequest|PRMergeAck|PRStatusUpdate|PRRequestRejected|DeadlockProbe|ReviewSLAAck|PreemptRequest|PreemptForce|MediationProposal|MediationAck|EscalationRequest|DECISION_REQUEST|DECISION_RESPONSE|DECISION_DEFER|DECISION_REJECT_FRAMING|HyperbriefCard|ULTRASAFE_FINDING|ULTRASAFE_ITERATION_BOUNDARY|ULTRASAFE_RELEASE_GATE|SECURITY_DISCLOSURE_INTAKE|MPCVD_COORDINATION)"'`. (Synced to ┬¦13.16.9 in v2.4.37: `AgentHello` moved to the noise blocklist per the handshake-group reclassification, and the Hyperbrief decision-delegation family, the Ultrasafe pre-release-pentest family, and `PRRequestRejected` added to the meaningful allowlist.) Why this matters: false-positive wake is still safer than false-negative miss (silent-stall class), but the cost is non-zero and the fix is two name-grep stages (noise-exclude then meaningful-match) ŌĆö ev-agnostic so it applies to every line in `inbox.log` regardless of which envelope format the line carries.

**Why ev was dropped from the filter (v2.4.16 correction)**: an earlier v2.4.2 form prepended a `grep '"ev":"inbound"'` 1st stage to the two name-based stages above. That form was correct for the **legacy event-relay format** (lines shaped `{"t":..., "ev":"inbound", "msg":{"name":...}}` that the bridge writes around its own lifecycle events ŌĆö `closed` / `ws-error` / `inbound` log entries from the bridge process) but a **hard fail for the direct inbound format** (lines shaped `{"at":..., "name":..., "value":..., "source":"agent"}` that the bridge writes when it actually delivers an A2A envelope from the server). The direct format has no `ev` field, so the ev-gate filtered it out entirely ŌĆö every bridge-alive inbound was silently dropped from the WAKE decision while the legacy lines (which carry no new A2A delivery) were the only thing the watcher could see. The diagnostic anchor: watchers `bv0u5h95p` (armed 02:19:31Z, base=518) and `bd7k7xoy3` (armed 02:32:49Z, base=518) both completed with REARM ~45min / "no meaningful inbound" while inbox lines 519~522 (3 main `Report` envelopes + 1 server `Ack`) arrived inside their armed windows in the direct format ŌĆö the ev-gate dropped all four before the name-stages ever saw them, and the agent was the last to know. Dropping the ev-stage is safe because the v2.4.2 intent (block self-emission echo + transport noise) was already carried entirely by the name blocklist; the ev-gate was redundant for the legacy format (the blocklist names cover both legacy `ev:"sent"` self-emission and direct self-emitted lines alike) and a hard fail for the direct format. Surfacing incidents: watcher `b1rrhbwo4` wake on 2026-05-31 caught the agent's own `WorkerReport` echo (self-emission) ŌĆö handled by the name blocklist; watcher `bbae2ph8r` wake later the same day caught a server `History` replay payload containing dozens of historical `Delegate` events from prior sessions (server-replay noise) ŌĆö also handled by the name blocklist; watchers `bv0u5h95p` + `bd7k7xoy3` REARM-timeout despite live direct-format inbound on 2026-06-01 ŌĆö the failure mode the v2.4.16 ev-stage drop eliminates.

**Board state real-time update ŌĆö the third turn-end ritual element**: alongside the inbox.log mtime probe and the unconditional watcher rearm, the agent MUST verify that the live-board `state.json` reflects the just-completed work *before* emitting the final response text. The board's `state.json` is the visualization SSoT for the human watching the live board (┬¦3); a turn that ticks done counters, completes a lane, or advances a current pointer in the agent's working memory but does NOT write that delta back into `state.json` leaves the board behind the agent's actual state ŌĆö the human sees a stale board while the agent has moved on. Concrete checklist at turn-end:

1. **`done` counter ticked** ŌĆö if the turn closed one or more PM/lane items, the `state.json` `done` count for the affected lane(s) reflects the new total.
2. **`current` pointer advanced** ŌĆö if the turn finished the item that was the live "current" focus, the `current` pointer either moves to the next item or clears (per the lane's idle convention).
3. **`updatedAt` bumped to wall-clock** ŌĆö the top-level `state.json.updatedAt` field is bumped to current wall-clock (ISO-Z), not left at the last write's timestamp. A stale `updatedAt` makes the dashboard's "last activity" indicator lie about the agent's real liveness.

This is a *discipline extension* to the turn-end ritual, not a new system: the existing ritual already covers watcher liveness (probe + rearm); board state real-time update covers the *board's* liveness from the human's perspective. The failure mode this addresses (observed upstream, 2026-05-31): main was observed to skip real-time board updates during multi-cycle work ŌĆö agent processed multiple lane items in a single turn, ticked them internally, but emitted only the final response without writing each delta to `state.json`. The live board drifted behind the agent's actual state for the duration of that multi-cycle turn; the human watching the board saw "main idle" or "main on item X" while the agent had already finished items X, Y, and was working on Z. Making the board-state update a turn-end ritual element ŌĆö same tier as inbox probe and watcher rearm ŌĆö removes the drift path: no response emission without a board-state verification pass.

**Planned queue scan ŌĆö the fifth turn-end ritual element**: alongside the four inbound/outbound-liveness elements above (inbox.log probe ┬Ę unconditional watcher rearm ┬Ę board state real-time update ┬Ę BOARD_STALE gate per ┬¦13.16.7), the agent MUST scan its **planned/pending work queue** at every turn-end *before* deciding whether to enter idle wait. The scan classifies each queue item:

- **`blocked`** ŌĆö waiting on main review, on a UI implementation the agent doesn't own, on a DB P1 the agent can't write, on an external PR landing, on any external dependency the agent CANNOT resolve from its own session. These items are *not progressable this turn*.
- **`planned` / `progressable`** ŌĆö P2/P3 fix pool, ┬¦13.16.6-style policy escalations the agent can draft itself, seed cascade work (master/lite/compact tiers), draft refinements that don't need user steering, doc sync follow-ups, any item the agent CAN progress without external input. These items are *progressable this turn*.

**The rule**: re-arm watcher (per the unconditional-spawn rule above) AND scan the planned queue. **If `planned` is non-empty ŌåÆ start the first `planned` item NOW, in the same turn, before emitting idle-wait.** Idle wait is reserved for true exhaustion: planned queue empty, OR every queue item classified `blocked`. The default presumption is *work continues* whenever a progressable item exists; idle wait is the exception, not the default.

**Why this belongs in the ritual, not just agent habit**: an agent absorbed in just-finished work tends to treat turn-end as "I'm done, wait for the next inbound" ŌĆö but in a healthy Constellation cadence the agent typically has multiple `planned` items at any moment, and entering idle wait while progressable work exists is a *self-inflicted stall* (the agent itself is the bottleneck, not external dependency). Making the queue scan a ritual element converts "remember to check what else I could be doing" from volitional habit into mechanical turn-end discipline ŌĆö same conversion ┬¦13.16.6's other ritual elements made for inbox/watcher/board liveness.

**Cross-link to Principle #16 (autonomous execution ŌĆö absolute)**: the planned-queue scan is the operational form of Principle #16 on the *turn-boundary* surface ŌĆö the seed-tier rule says "proceed without escalating when the gate set doesn't fire", and the ritual element says "at every turn-end, the gate-set check is mechanically run against the entire planned queue, not just the just-finished item". ┬¦13.18 (non-branching choices) covers the choice-emission surface of the same principle; this fifth ritual element covers the queue-consumption surface.

**Provenance**: adopted 2026-05-31. Originating context: the planned-vs-blocked distinction surfaced alongside the conditionalŌåÆunconditional rearm correction in the same dogfood turn, both as escalations of ┬¦13.16.6 turn-end ritual to absolute-discipline tier.

**Composition with the other four elements**: **element 1 (cursor-tail probe) is the FIRST mandatory step** ŌĆö it catches inbound that already landed below the new watcher's `base` (the armed-window blind spot, structurally invisible to any watcher armed after the inbound arrived); this is the PRIMARY catch mechanism for inbound that landed during the prior watcher's suspend window. **Element 2 (unconditional rearm) is the second mandatory step** ŌĆö it is the forward-looking catch mechanism for inbound that will land during the next idle window; it does NOT recover inbound below its own `base`. The probe and the rearm cover *disjoint* windows (the probe covers the past gap, the rearm covers the future window); both are required, in this order, every turn. Board-state real-time update prevents the *board* from going stale relative to the agent's actual state (outbound-side liveness, from the human's perspective); BOARD_STALE gate (┬¦13.16.7) mechanizes the board-update discipline as a watcher-side fail-safe (NOT a substitute for the agent-side update, just a backstop when the agent-side discipline fails); planned queue scan prevents the agent from *self-stalling* when progressable work exists (queue-consumption liveness, from the work-pipeline perspective). All five are required ŌĆö the inbound-side pair (probe + rearm, in order) ensures the agent doesn't miss what arrives, the outbound-side pair ensures the human sees the agent's actual progress, and the queue scan ensures the agent doesn't idle while it still has work it can do. Provenance: adopted 2026-05-31 (elements 1-3, then element 4 via the ┬¦13.16.7 amendment, then element 5); ordering reinforcement (element 1 strictly before element 2) ŌĆö a same-day incident (the agent missed two inbound reports by running rearm before probe).

**Pre-large-work context materialization ŌĆö the sixth turn-end ritual element**: alongside the five inbound/outbound/queue-liveness elements above (inbox.log probe ┬Ę unconditional watcher rearm ┬Ę board state real-time update ┬Ę BOARD_STALE gate ┬Ę planned-queue scan), the agent MUST ŌĆö **BEFORE entering any large multi-cycle work** (workflow chains, multi-commit sequences, design RRPs, multi-section spec drafts, cross-tier seed cascades, anything that may span more than one compact-boundary's worth of token budget) ŌĆö **materialize the in-context working set to durable artifacts** the post-compact future-self can pick up cold. The materialization is concrete, not aspirational:

1. **Identify the work scope** ŌĆö a one-line title and a one-paragraph rationale that says what is being attempted and why (the *intent* layer, the part that disappears first when context resets).
2. **List the files and line ranges to touch** ŌĆö every file the work plans to edit, every section anchor (`┬¦13.x.y` / function name / heading) the work plans to modify or add. Concrete paths and concrete anchors ŌĆö not "the Constellation file" but a symbol/heading anchor like `Constellation.md ┬¦13.16.6` (the turn-end ritual checklist) or a function name, never a brittle line number.
3. **Name the EG-side outputs** ŌĆö RRP file path, PM ledger entry, WORKLIST queue item, `state.json` snapshot key, spec anchor ŌĆö the durable artifact(s) that will carry the work across the context boundary. Each artifact gets a stable identifier (RRP filename, PM lane + ordinal, WORKLIST `id`) so the post-compact agent can locate it by name, not by recall.
4. **Anchor the design decisions in a written doc** ŌĆö every non-obvious choice (option-X-over-Y rationales, tradeoffs already adjudicated, ruled-out alternatives) lands in the RRP / spec / PM-entry **before** the multi-cycle work begins, not as a follow-up after compact. Decisions in context but not in artifact are *lost decisions* ŌĆö they evaporate at the next compact and the post-compact self re-litigates them, often differently.

The end state of element 6 is that the work is **pickable cold**: a future-self instance with zero in-context memory of the planning could open the named artifact(s), read the scope + file-list + decisions, and resume the multi-cycle work without re-deriving anything. If element 6 cannot produce that pickable-cold state, the multi-cycle work has NOT yet been authorized to begin ŌĆö the materialization is the *entry gate* for large work, not a post-hoc note. **This element is the structural mechanism that makes ┬¦13.21 (fresh-context defer is anti-pattern) operative**: ┬¦13.21 says the agent must RESUME after compact rather than defer; element 6 is what makes resume *possible*, by ensuring the resume target exists as a durable artifact rather than as an evaporated in-context memory. Provenance: adopted 2026-05-31.

**Composition with the other five elements (extended to six)**: elements 1-5 cover the *turn-boundary* surface (inbound-side ┬Ę outbound-side ┬Ę queue-consumption); element 6 covers the *compact-boundary* surface (cross-context-reset liveness). The turn boundary fires every user-facing response; the compact boundary fires opaquely when the harness decides to compact (typically token-budget-threshold-driven, not agent-driven). Elements 1-5 keep one turn's transitions clean; element 6 keeps multi-turn / multi-cycle work survivable across the compact that may fire in the middle of it. All six are required; none absorbs the others.

**Mechanization (v2.4.14) ŌĆö pre-compact hook pair + handoff file**: element 6 names the discipline; harness hooks can mechanize the halves a deterministic script *can* own. Reference implementation at `constellation/reference/runtime/pre-compact/`: (a) **`pre-compact-snapshot.cjs`** runs as a `PreCompact` hook (matcher `*` ŌĆö both auto and manual compaction) and snapshots the *environment* truth (git HEAD / dirty files / latest tag, optional secondary repo + track-doc listing) into a handoff file, emitting `additionalContext` that directs the post-compact agent to read it; (b) **`reload-handoff.cjs`** runs as a `SessionStart` hook with matcher `"compact"` and prints the handoff file to stdout, which the harness injects into the fresh context ŌĆö the re-entry half. The handoff file has two zones: an **auto-snapshot block** (marker-delimited, machine-replaced) and a **standing card** the *model* maintains ŌĆö procedure details that compaction summaries reliably drop (env-var call conventions, routing rules, policy one-liners, active background-task/workflow IDs + resume handles). The standing card is the part no deterministic script can collect ŌĆö populate it via a pre-compact skill or as part of element 6 materialization before large work; keep it short (the whole file re-enters context, so its length is a recurring tax). Division of labor: hooks own the environment + re-injection; the model owns the judgment of *which in-context details are load-bearing*. Observed failure mode this closes (2026-06-11): a routing convention (an env-var prefix required on one script call) lived only in-context, was dropped by a compaction summary, and the post-compact agent reverted to the script's default path ŌĆö misrouting five A2A messages to the wrong board until a human noticed downstream.

**Threshold-armed continuous handoff ŌĆö the handoff-guard mode (v2.4.68)**: the v2.4.14 hook pair fires *at* the compact boundary; the handoff card's freshness at that moment still depends on when the model last ran the before-compact discipline ŌĆö an **auto**-compact can land on a card many work-cycles stale. The handoff-guard turns the discipline continuous once it matters. A **turn-end (Stop) hook** (reference: `constellation/reference/runtime/pre-compact/context-watch.cjs`) measures context usage from the session transcript ŌĆö the harness does not expose context% to hooks, but the transcript's per-assistant-turn API usage does: the last **non-sidechain** assistant entry's input + cache-read + cache-creation + output tokens (sidechain entries are subagent contexts, not the main window) ŌĆö against a **declared window** (config, default 200k) raised by the **session's max observed context**, which is a hard lower bound of the true window (context can never exceed it) and so self-corrects an under-declared window on large-context models; the observed floor resets per session id. Below the threshold (default **0.75**) the hook is silent, and falling back below ŌĆö i.e. compaction ŌĆö disarms the mode automatically. At or above it, the hook requires the handoff card to have been touched **during the just-finished turn** (card mtime vs the previous turn-end baseline): satisfied ŌåÆ pass with a status systemMessage; not satisfied ŌåÆ **block exactly once** with instructions ŌĆö the first crossing asks for the full before-compact pass, later turns ask only for the turn's delta ŌĆö and never re-blocks within the same stop chain (`stop_hook_active` loop guard). Soft-strong by design: exactly one nudge per turn, no infinite loop, and a model that ignores the nudge still terminates. Config `.agent/context-watch.json` `{enabled, threshold, window, handoffPath}` (absent file = defaults ŌĆö registering the hook is the opt-in; `enabled:false` disables without unregistering); state `.agent/.context-watch-state.json` (git-ignored). Portability: the contract is three surfaces ŌĆö a turn-end hook point, transcript-visible per-turn usage, and a card-mtime gate ŌĆö any harness with those implements it identically.


**Armed-window blind spot ŌĆö the real fail mode of 2026-05-31**: an *earlier diagnosis* in this section attributed the missed seq 85 to harness GC of bash-bg watchers (the 38-byte output of `bc6tfgw2d` + `bd48j8vrj` read as an "abnormal exit signature"). That diagnosis was **wrong**. Re-reading those task outputs after both completed: the 38 bytes was the `re-armed @ <Z> base=<N>` header ŌĆö the watcher was polling normally during a no-inbound window ŌĆö and the actual second line `REARM: ~45min, no meaningful inbound` was appended only when the 45-minute timeout fired. *Both watchers were alive the entire time; both exited cleanly via timeout.* The real cause of the seq 85 miss is structural, not a process-lifecycle failure:

The watcher's `base=<line count>` cursor only watches *new* inbound that arrives **after** spawn. Any inbound that arrived **before** the watcher armed is below the cursor and is permanently invisible to that watcher and all subsequent watchers. On 2026-05-31: agent processed the "D" user reply ŌåÆ dispatched Workflow 6 with no mid-turn watcher ŌåÆ seq 85 arrived (02:05Z, line 292) during this gap ŌåÆ next watcher (`bfnmb8e09`) armed @ 02:08Z with `base=292`, watching only line >292 ŌåÆ seq 85 sat at line 292 forever, invisible. This is the **armed-window blind spot**: any inbound that lands between the *previous turn's watcher exit* and the *next watcher's spawn* falls into a black hole.

**The fix that closes the gap ŌĆö cursor-based unread tail** (agent main loop responsibility, not the watcher's): the agent maintains a *last-surfaced line cursor* across turns (the highest inbox.log line number it has actually read into context). At every turn-start AND every turn-end, the agent tails `inbox.log` from that cursor (NOT from the watcher's `base`), surfaces any meaningful inbound it finds, and advances the cursor. This catches the in-between-watchers inbound the watcher itself cannot. Composition with the watcher rules: the watcher catches *new* arrivals during a wait; the cursor tail catches *missed* arrivals from gaps in watcher coverage. Both are required.

**Wall-clock vs task-clock mismatch ŌĆö the secondary cause of the blind window**: in addition to the structural `base` cursor gap above, observation across 8 watcher cycles on 2026-05-31 confirmed the bash bg task's clock and the wall clock diverge. Watchers armed for a `MAX = 540 ├Ś 5s = 2700s = 45min` polling budget reliably reported `REARM: ~45min, no meaningful inbound` only after ~55ŌĆō60 minutes of wall-clock ŌĆö a ~10ŌĆō15 min surplus. The most consistent explanation: the harness `SIGSTOP`s bg tasks while the agent's foreground turn is active and `SIGCONT`s them when the turn ends, so `sleep N` in the watcher does not advance during agent-active windows. Consequence: a watcher whose polling logically *should* be sweeping the inbox is in fact paused during exactly the windows when the agent is busy enough that inbound might land ŌĆö the agent-active window IS the blind window. The cursor-tail fix is the structural answer; the bg-task pause is the mechanism that makes the gap inevitable, not a separate failure to mitigate.

**Defunct earlier mitigations** (kept here briefly for the commit-history record): the redundant-watcher rule (5s + 7s pair) was proposed under the GC-kill diagnosis and does NOT address the armed-window blind spot ŌĆö two watchers armed at the same `base` have the same blind spot, not a complementary one. Cron fallback (Claude Code `CronCreate` every 15-30 min) remains useful as a long-idle safety net (it gets the agent to *some* turn-start where the cursor tail can run), but it is not the primary fix either. The primary fix is the cursor tail in the agent main loop. Surfacing incident, corrected: 2026-05-31 user message `"ņ×¼ļ¼┤ņ×źņØ┤ ļśÉ ĒÆĆļĀĖļäż"` ŌĆö initial diagnosis (GC-kill) was wrong; correct diagnosis is the armed-window blind spot. The earlier paragraph's `bc6tfgw2d` / `bd48j8vrj` 38-byte output was normal polling, not abnormal exit.

**Element 2 timing ŌĆö settled at turn-end mandatory rearm (lock-in against further flip-flop)**: the ┬¦13.16.6 element 2 execution point went through a brief sequence of revisions (a turn-end ŌåÆ next-cycle-start refinement, a revert back to turn-end, a re-application of the next-cycle-start form, and a final revert) before settling on **turn-end mandatory rearm**. The reason turn-end is correct is structural, not stylistic: the inter-cycle gap (from current turn-end to the arrival of the next user-input) must have an armed watcher throughout, because inbound that lands during that gap is exactly the class of message a deferred rearm cannot catch ŌĆö a watcher scheduled to spawn at next-cycle start is not yet alive during the gap, and any inbound arriving in that window lands without a watcher to wake on it, producing the silent-stall failure mode this section exists to prevent. The ┬¦13.21 composition rules the same way: deferring the rearm step to next-cycle start IS a cross-cycle deferral of work that the current cycle owes, which is the exact pattern ┬¦13.21 forbids. An earlier reading framed next-cycle-start placement as "structural location, not deferral", but that reading missed where the structural correct location actually is ŌĆö the structural location of the watcher that catches inter-cycle inbound is BEFORE the inter-cycle gap begins, which means at current turn-end. The cost-asymmetry argument confirms the same choice: concurrent-watcher-overlap that the next-cycle-start form tried to avoid is harmless (FP cost = one task slot + a few log lines), while the cost of a watcherless inter-cycle gap is hours of silently missed inbound (FN cost catastrophic) ŌĆö pay the trivial FP cost every turn to avoid the catastrophic FN cost. This paragraph is the lock-in: turn-end mandatory rearm is the settled discipline for element 2, and any future proposal to relocate the rearm away from turn-end must first demonstrate how the inter-cycle gap is otherwise covered, which the next-cycle-start form did not.

#### 13.16.7 BOARD_STALE gate ŌĆö pre-rearm board freshness check

**The gate** (mechanization of ┬¦13.16.6's third turn-end ritual element ŌĆö board state real-time update): at the *start* of every watcher re-arm cycle, before entering the polling loop, the watcher compares the git HEAD commit time against the last commit time that touched `state.json`. Concretely: `git log -1 HEAD --format=%ct` (the working tree's tip commit epoch) versus `git log -1 -- state.json --format=%ct` (the most recent commit that included a `state.json` change). The gate **fires** when HEAD's commit time is *strictly greater than* the state.json commit time ŌĆö i.e. there exists at least one commit after the last board-refresh commit that did not refresh the board. The gate **passes** when the two are equal ŌĆö i.e. the most recent HEAD commit itself included the `state.json` update, so the board is current as of HEAD. When the gate fires, the watcher does NOT re-arm; it exits immediately with a `WAKE(BOARD_STALE)` event surfaced into the watcher's task output (and into `inbox.log` as a self-emitted wake marker, per the ┬¦13.16.6 self-emission filter discipline). The next turn-start will read the wake, the agent will write the missing `state.json` deltas and commit them, and only then will a fresh watcher arm. **No time buffer, no env-configurable threshold** ŌĆö the comparison is identity-based on commit ancestry, not offset-based on wall-clock.

**Why mechanize, not just discipline**: ┬¦13.16.6 already specifies the board-state update as the third turn-end ritual element, and that rule is correct. But discipline based on agent volition was observed to fail **twice** (2026-05-31) when the agent was absorbed in multi-cycle work (workflow chain + commit pipeline + follow-up patches) ŌĆö the very absorption that makes the rule necessary is the same absorption that makes volitional compliance unreliable. Volitional discipline does not survive the absorbed state. Moving the check off the agent's turn-end ritual and onto the watcher's re-arm path converts the failure mode from "agent forgets to update board ŌåÆ board drifts indefinitely until human notices" into "watcher refuses to re-arm ŌåÆ agent is forced to update board on the next wake, at the latest within one rearm-interval cycle". The gate cannot be forgotten because the agent is not the one running it.

**Scope ŌĆö main only**: the gate runs only when the watcher's `agentId === WS_PRIMARY_AGENT` (i.e. the main agent that owns the live-board `state.json` write). Workers do NOT own `state.json` ŌĆö their outbound is `WorkerReport` to the main inbox, and the board reflects worker progress via main's relay write ŌĆö so a worker watcher's HEAD-vs-state-commit-time comparison would be meaningless (workers commit to their own worktrees on their own cadence, unrelated to the board's `state.json` history). Worker watchers skip the BOARD_STALE check and re-arm normally.

**Self-trap-avoidance rationale ŌĆö why no time buffer**: an earlier draft of this section used a 120 s time-buffer rule (`headEpoch ŌłÆ stateUpdatedAtEpoch > 120 s` fires the gate). That draft **self-trapped**: the board-refresh commit itself takes wall-clock time to author (commit hook + push + any in-flight workflow), which moves HEAD's commit epoch past the `state.json.updatedAt` value the agent just wrote ŌĆö by a margin equal to the workflow's wall-clock cost. Any workflow longer than the buffer (and many normal multi-cycle workflows easily exceed 120 s) would therefore keep `headEpoch ŌłÆ updatedAt > 120 s` even immediately after a correct, conscientious board refresh, leaving the gate fired forever and the watcher refusing to re-arm despite the board being current. The fix is to switch from an *offset-based* comparison (wall-clock delta against a tolerance) to an *identity-based* comparison (commit ancestry: did the latest HEAD commit include `state.json`?). With the head-vs-state-commit-time form, the board-refresh commit advances both `git log -1 HEAD --format=%ct` and `git log -1 -- state.json --format=%ct` to the *same* value in lockstep ŌĆö the very act of refreshing the board passes the gate, because the refresh commit IS the HEAD commit that touched `state.json`. There is no wall-clock margin to overshoot, so no self-trap.

**Composition with ┬¦13.16.6**: the third turn-end ritual element (board state real-time update) remains the *primary* control ŌĆö the agent should still verify the board reflects the just-completed work *before* emitting the final response. The BOARD_STALE gate is the **safety net** that catches the case where the primary control fails (agent absorbed in multi-cycle work, forgot the ritual). Same two-layer pattern as inbox liveness: probe (┬¦13.16.6, agent-side) is primary, turn-end mandatory rearm (┬¦13.16.6.1 ritual) is the safety net; here, turn-end board update is primary, BOARD_STALE re-arm gate is the safety net. Both layers required for the same reason: the primary control is the right thing to do every turn, the safety net is what saves the cycle when the primary fails.

**Cross-references**: ┬¦13.16.6 (board state real-time update ŌĆö the discipline this gate mechanizes; especially the "third turn-end ritual element" and "Composition with the other two elements" paragraphs), ┬¦13.16.6's turn-end ritual paragraphs (the gate is the new pre-rearm hook on the rearm half of the ritual), and `constellation/self-wake-watcher.eux` (the watcher spec where the `@machine` state diagram retains the `BOARD_STALE` exit state alongside the existing `WAKE` / `REARM` / `IDLE` states; the gate fires on the `IDLE ŌåÆ arming` transition, and the `@machine` guard is now `headCommitTime > stateLastCommitTime` ŌĆö i.e. `git log -1 HEAD --format=%ct` strictly greater than `git log -1 -- state.json --format=%ct`, with equality meaning the latest HEAD commit included the board refresh and the gate passes).

**Retired prior version ŌĆö 120 s time-buffer**: the earlier draft of this section used a 120 s time-buffer rule (`headEpoch ŌłÆ stateUpdatedAtEpoch > 120 s`) with a `CONSTELLATION_BOARD_STALE_THRESHOLD_S` env knob. That version self-trapped: the board-refresh commit itself moves `headEpoch` past `updatedAt` by a wall-clock margin equal to the workflow's duration, so any workflow longer than the buffer kept the gate fired forever even after a correct refresh. Retired in favor of head-vs-state-commit-time identity comparison (no buffer, no env var, no self-trap). The main-only filter (`agentId === WS_PRIMARY_AGENT`) and worker exemption are unchanged across versions.

**Provenance**: adopted 2026-05-31, amended same day; the original gate shipped with the now-retired 120 s buffer.

#### 13.16.8 A2A communication priority discipline ŌĆö outbound messages (and their prerequisites) take priority over other planned actions

**The discipline**: whenever an external state change occurs ŌĆö user steering, a newly-arrived task, an external event (counterpart `Delegate` / `Report` / `Status` / `BlockerNudge` inbound, cycle restart with a queued plan) ŌĆö and the resulting work plan contains at least one outbound A2A message to a counterpart agent (e.g., outbox push to `main`, `Delegate` to a worker, `Report` back to a requester, `BlockerManifest` emission), the agent MUST execute the following ordering: (1) **scan the new plan's action list and identify every action that is itself an outbound A2A message** to a counterpart; (2) **also identify the prerequisite work that the counterpart needs in order to act on the message** ŌĆö any commit-push of referenced docs the counterpart will fetch (a `Delegate` payload that points to a doc URL is unusable until the doc is reachable at that URL), any payload that needs assembling, any `state.json` or live-board update the counterpart's decision depends on; (3) **move both the message itself and its prerequisite work to the head of the action queue**, ahead of any other planned action; (4) only after the message has been emitted do the remaining planned actions proceed.

**Two technical rationales**:

(a) **Drift-containment**. If the EG side updates a spec, a state field, or a doc *before* notifying the counterpart, the counterpart continues operating on a now-stale baseline for the entire duration of the unnotified gap. Any work the counterpart performs in that gap risks landing on a superseded baseline ŌĆö wasted effort, divergent artifacts, follow-up reconciliation cost. Sending the message first ŌĆö even while other local actions remain queued ŌĆö lets the counterpart pause, redirect, or re-fetch at the earliest possible moment. The drift window collapses from "EG's local-work duration" to "round-trip latency", which is typically orders of magnitude smaller and bounded by transport, not by EG's queue depth.

(b) **Counterpart-start-time minimization**. When the new plan obligates the counterpart to start a piece of work ŌĆö e.g., "main runs DB benchmarking starting from Mode B entry", "worker takes over the reference-runtime cp track", "collab reviews the new RRP" ŌĆö every minute EG spends on local actions before emitting the trigger is a minute the counterpart hasn't started. Total wall-clock to cycle completion is `message-emit-time + counterpart-work-duration`; advancing the emit time directly shortens the cycle. Local EG actions that don't gate the message can happen in parallel with the counterpart's work once the message is out, but cannot recover the head-start lost by emitting the message late.

**Symmetry**: the discipline applies to any role classified by ┬¦13.16 (`main` / `local` / `collab` / `upstream`) when that role initiates a cross-agent change. A worker reporting back to main, main delegating to a worker, EG reporting back to an upstream collaborator, an upstream agent steering a downstream ŌĆö all four directions follow the same priority rule. The rule is about *the act of initiating a cross-agent state change*, not about who initiates it.

**Composition with existing ┬¦13.x ŌĆö no override of orthogonal gates**:

- **┬¦13.14 redaction** still gates the message *content* (placeholder substitution for non-public identifiers, technical-only phrasing). The priority rule decides *when* the message goes; ┬¦13.14 decides *what's in it*. Both apply; neither bypasses the other.
- **┬¦13.17 main-chat structured-choice ban** still gates the message *destination* (board-mediated route for structured Q/A, no inline option UI in main-chat). The priority rule does not authorize routing a structured choice into main-chat just because it's the head-of-queue item; the ┬¦13.17 routing decision is made first, then the chosen destination's emission is what gets priority.
- **┬¦13.20 BlockerManifest emission**: a blocker that triggers a `BlockerManifest` is itself an outbound A2A communication and gets the same priority as any other A2A message. When a turn-end ritual identifies a blocker that needs `BlockerManifest` emission *and* the plan also contains other actions, the emission goes first.
- **Destructive-operation authorization gates** are not bypassed: if the prerequisite work for a message is itself a destructive operation (e.g., a force-push the counterpart will need to fetch), the destructive-operation authorization path still applies. The priority rule reorders the queue; it does not relax authorization requirements.

**Composition with ┬¦13.16.6 turn-end ritual ŌĆö independent schedule**: the cursor-tail probe (element 1) and the unconditional watcher rearm (element 2) run on their own schedule ŌĆö every turn-end, regardless of whether the current plan contains an outbound message.
