- **Seed Principle #16** (autonomous execution ŌĆö absolute) ŌĆö the seed-tier anchor. ┬¦13.21 is the explicit operational form of Principle #16 for the *time-surface* (context-boundary defer), the same way ┬¦13.18 is the operational form for the *choice-surface* (non-branching solicit) and ┬¦13.16.6 element 5 is the operational form for the *queue-surface* (idle-while-progressable). All three surfaces share the same principle; ┬¦13.21 closes the time-surface defection path.

**Provenance**: adopted 2026-05-31. Originating context: the fresh-context defer pattern surfaced in dogfood as the remaining escape from autonomous execution ŌĆö even after ┬¦13.18 (recommend+proceed) and ┬¦13.16.6 element 5 (planned-queue scan / #442) closed the choice-emission and queue-consumption surfaces, the agent could still defer planned work to "next context" and self-permission idle-wait via that phrasing. ┬¦13.21 closes that surface; ┬¦13.16.6 element 6 is the paired structural enabler that makes the resume-rather-than-defer rule meetable in practice.

### 13.22 A2A PR System ŌĆö cross-repo pull request orchestration (two-level, layered above ┬¦13.13)

The Constellation A2A wire (┬¦2) + ack layer (┬¦13.13) + role model (┬¦13.9) make cross-repo pull-request coordination *possible*, but without a wire vocabulary for the PR lifecycle the manual step in the middle of an otherwise-automated mirror pipeline ŌĆö a human opening the provider UI, copying the body, picking the branch, and creating the PR ŌĆö remains a per-event chore that scales linearly with cross-repo spec-parity events. ┬¦13.22 is the formal spec that closes that gap: a **wire vocabulary + agent topology + state machine** treatment (NOT a script) that surfaces the full PR lifecycle as A2A `CUSTOM` types, so the live board, the ┬¦13.13 ack discipline, the ┬¦13.19 deadlock detector, and the ┬¦13.20 blocker tracker all compose over PR state. It is layered *above* ┬¦13.13 (it does not modify the wire shape or the ack grades) and *composes with* ┬¦13.9 (authority), ┬¦13.17 (decisions panel), ┬¦13.19 (quasi-deadlock), and ┬¦13.20 (blocker nudge).

#### 13.22.1 Status & provenance

- **Status**: formal spec (P1 ŌĆö EG 1ņ░©ņ¦ĆņŗØ contract; Constellation orchestration domain). Distilled from the RRP draft into the adopted Phase 1 + Phase 1b form.
- **Inputs** (cited, not republished): **EG RRP** ŌĆö `constellation/reference/docs/archive/2026-06-01-a2a-pr-system-rrp.md` (the in-repo design doc; carries the two-level abstraction, the five-type wire vocabulary, the topology analysis, the approval-category model, the cross-repo content-sourcing options, the per-repo authority model, the 5-state lifecycle, and the dogfood-validated bridge invariants ŌĆö including the v0.3 dogfood learnings: `sourceContentRef.kind` enum, `inline-section-mirror` semantics, `targetPath` base, cherry-pick skip, dry-run `abs+exists` gate, `trusted_mirrors` alias resolve). The reference implementation of the PR-bot path lives at the adopter/hub side (local-bridge `createPR` port + server-side five-type observer + `wsPrMergeReject` strict gate); EG ships the protocol spec + the RRP doc, not the bridge impl.
- **Layering invariant**: ┬¦13.22 sits *above* ┬¦13.13 (every PR-lifecycle emission gets server-auto `Ack{delivered}`) and *uses* ┬¦13.9 (per-repo role mapping for the merge-authority gate). It does NOT modify ┬¦2 (the wire shape), the ┬¦13.13 ack grades (`delivered`/`processed`), or the ┬¦13.11 board-emission discipline. The five new `CUSTOM` types sit on top of those layers.
- **Redaction discipline (┬¦13.14)**: the target production hub is referred to as `<hub-repo>`; the real repo identifier lives only in operator-local `state.json` (or is derived at runtime from `git remote get-url origin`) and never appears on the A2A wire. The EG repo (`SoliEstre/EstreGenesis`) is named explicitly because it is public-shipped.

#### 13.22.2 Two-level abstraction ŌĆö Level 1 (virtual PR, A2A-only) vs Level 2 (Github PR, provider-mediated)

The same wire vocabulary (┬¦13.22.3) and state machine (┬¦13.22.8) describe two physical realizations of a "PR." Which applies is a function of *who operates the source and target sides* and *what file-system access the receiving side holds*. `PRRequest.level` is an explicit `1 | 2` payload field; it defaults to `2` when absent.

- **Level 1 ŌĆö virtual PR (A2A-only path)**. No provider-side PR object is created. Applicable when source and target sides **share an operator** AND **both hold direct repo-level file-system access**. The receiving side (holding commit-push authority on the target repo) reads the `sourceContentRef` carried by `PRRequest`, applies the change directly to its local checkout of the target repo, commits, and pushes ŌĆö using A2A envelopes only for review / ack signaling. `gh pr create` is skipped; MERGED ŌēĪ "commit pushed to the target's integration branch."
- **Level 2 ŌĆö Github PR (provider-mediated path)**. The receiving side invokes `gh pr create` against the target provider; the PR exists as a real provider object; review and merge flow through the provider UI / API, with A2A envelopes mirroring state. Applicable when source and target are operated by different parties, OR the PR is cross-org, OR the target's integration policy requires a provider-side PR object (required-status-checks, provider-tier audit trail).

**Selection rule**. When `category == trusted-mirror` AND operator-shares-target AND target-repo-direct-access both hold, **Level 1 is the default**; otherwise Level 2. The receiving side MUST validate the requested `level` against its capability matrix (direct push to `targetRepo`? operator-shared?) and MUST reject a mismatch with a capability-mismatch reason; the sender MAY retry with the other level. The ┬¦13.22.8 state machine is `level`-discriminated: both levels traverse the same five logical states, but the transition triggers and the MERGED realization differ.

#### 13.22.3 Wire vocabulary ŌĆö five new CUSTOM types

Five new `CUSTOM` types, all layered above ┬¦13.13 (server-stamped `msgId`, server-auto `Ack{delivered}`, recipient `AckProcessed`). All are application-tier emissions ŌĆö none server-auto-emitted. All apply to both levels; per-type level-discriminated fields flagged inline.

| Name | Direction | Required fields | Optional fields | Server filter / authority gate |
|------|-----------|-----------------|-----------------|--------------------------------|
| `PRRequest` | any agent ŌåÆ PR-bot / repo-owner agent | `sourceRepo`, `sourceContentRef`, `targetRepo`, `targetBranch`, `title`, `body`, `level: 1\|2` (default `2`) | `labels[]`, `reviewers[]`, `category`, `slaEta` | Validates repos in the known-repo registry; for `level==1`, validates the receiver's capability matrix |
| `PRDraftReady` | PR-bot (L2) / receiving-side (L1) ŌåÆ requester | `for: msgId`, `draftRef`, `checksPending[]` | `prUrl` (L2), `headBranch`, `dryRun` | Validates `for` references a real `PRRequest` from a registered requester |
| `PRReviewAck` | reviewer-role agent ŌåÆ requester | `for: draftRef`, `verdict: approve\|request-changes\|comment`, `reviewBody` | `inlineComments[]`, `slaEta`, `reviewedAt` | Validates emitter role against the per-repo reviewer policy |
| `PRMergeRequest` / `PRMergeAck` | merge-authority ŌåÆ PR-bot / receiving-side; back to requester | `for: draftRef`, `mergeStrategy` (L2) | `commitTitle`, `deleteSourceBranch`, `dryRun` | `PRMergeRequest`: **strict** ŌĆö only `role==main` for the target repo; non-main rejected + logged to `decisions` |
| `PRStatusUpdate` | PR-bot (L2) / receiving-side (L1) ŌåÆ watchers | `draftRef`, `level`, `state: draft\|open\|changes_requested\|approved\|merged\|closed` | `checks` (L2), `reviewState`, `nextSlaCheckAt` | Validates emitter against bot-identity registry (L2) / capability matrix (L1) |

**`sourceContentRef.kind` enum** (closed ŌĆö receivers MUST reject unknown values): `branch-ref` (`git fetch` + `checkout FETCH_HEAD -- .`), `inline-files-diff` (`git apply <filesDiff>`), `inline-section-mirror` (apply `body` to `targetPath` per `mergeStrategy`, then `git add <targetPath>` ONLY, commit ŌĆö NO branch-fetch). **Fail-safe** (load-bearing): unrecognized `kind` ŌåÆ reject with `PRRequestRejected { reason: 'unknown-source-content-kind', kind }`, MUST NOT fall through to a default (an unknown kind falling through to `branch-ref` triggers `checkout FETCH_HEAD -- .` = wholesale target-repo overwrite ŌĆö the dogfood near-disaster).

#### 13.22.4 Agent topology ŌĆö local-bridge command (adopted)

Three realizations of the PR-bot role: **(a) Dedicated A2A agent** (long-running `pr-bot` holding provider credentials; clean isolation but needs a credential store + deploy surface); **(b) Local-bridge command ŌĆö ADOPTED** (extend `local-bridge` with a `createPR` port running in the operator's IDE alongside their `gh`/`git` auth ŌĆö no separate credentials; the flow: agent emits `PRRequest` ŌåÆ local-bridge invokes provider CLI [L2] or applies-commits-pushes locally [L1] ŌåÆ emits `PRDraftReady`); **(c) Hybrid** (dedicated bot for cross-machine/separate-identity, local-bridge for same-operator; deferred). Topology (b) is adopted because it reuses the operator's existing CLI auth ŌĆö no credential store in scope. It is also the natural home for **Level 1**: the bridge already holds direct file-system access on both sides when they share an operator. Topology (a)/(c) are phase-2/3 expansions (a credential-management RRP gates (a)).

#### 13.22.5 Approval discipline ŌĆö trusted-mirror / standard (per-PR opt-in default) / emergency

The autonomous-execution external-publish gate is canonical: a PR to a repo other than the one the agent operates in is an external publish requiring user opt-in *unless* a pre-authorized policy specifies otherwise.

- **`trusted-mirror`** (pre-authorized) ŌĆö a spec-mirror PR where the diff is *already reviewed in the source repo* and the target is *the deterministic mirror surface*. The pre-authorization lives in `state.json.pr_system.trusted_mirrors[]` as `(sourceRepo, sourceContentRef) ŌåÆ (targetRepo, targetContentRef)` pairings. A matching `PRRequest { category: 'trusted-mirror' }` is created without per-PR prompt; per-deployment policy MAY rate-limit (Ōēż1 per pair per 24h) to catch runaway automation.
- **`standard`** (per-PR user opt-in ŌĆö **the default**) ŌĆö any PR not matching a trusted-mirror entry. The receiving side surfaces the request via the live board `decisions` panel (┬¦13.17 ŌĆö the canonical structured-choice surface); the user explicitly approves; on approval the PR is created. This is the external-publish gate's default.
- **`emergency`** (out-of-band approval reference) ŌĆö for hotfix mirrors faster than the user can respond; carries `outOfBandApprovalRef` (a `decisions` msgId the user pre-approved), validated against the board's persistence. Carries a TOCTOU risk surface; **deferred to phase 3**. Phase 1/1b ship `trusted-mirror` + `standard` only.

**`inline-section-mirror` invariants** (the canonical spec-mirror content form): (1) **`git add` isolation** ŌĆö after applying `body`, `git add <targetPath>` ONLY, never `-A`/`.` (a fallthrough commits every untracked file ŌĆö the dogfood defect); (2) **No branch-fetch**; (3) **Existence check** ŌĆö verify `targetPath` exists before append, else reject `inline-mirror-target-missing`; (4) **Dry-run `abs+exists` log** ŌĆö when gated OFF, log `abs=<resolved> exists=<bool>` so path defects surface pre-live. **`targetPath` base** = relative to the receiver's repo root (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`), deterministic + portable; process-cwd / absolute / sub-tree bases are NOT used.

#### 13.22.6 Cross-repo content sourcing ŌĆö ╬▓ŌĆ▓ mirror-branch-on-target (adopted) + ╬▒ small-diff fallback

- **╬▓ŌĆ▓ ŌĆö mirror branch on the TARGET repo (Level 2 primary, adopted)**. Instead of pushing a branch to the source repo and fetching cross-repo, the local-bridge pushes source content to a `mirror/<topic>` branch on the **target** repo, then opens the PR from that target-side mirror branch into the target's integration branch ŌĆö effectively intra-repo at the provider level, no cross-repo provider authorization. (Trade-off: requires push access to the target repo; the mirror branch is transient, relying on provider auto-delete-head-branch.)
- **╬▒ ŌĆö inline diff (small-diff fallback)**. Unified-diff bytes in `PRRequest.filesDiff`, applied by the receiver. Used only for small Level-2 diffs (< ~50 KB); breaks at scale (~80 KB+ outbox split-delivery).
- **╬▓ (source-repo branch) / ╬│ (fork) NOT used** in scope ŌĆö ╬▓ŌĆ▓ supersedes ╬▓ (sidesteps cross-repo provider read-auth). **Level 1** sourcing is implicit (receiver reads `sourceContentRef` directly; no mirror branch). **`trusted_mirrors.targetRepo` alias** ŌĆö the registry SHOULD use a stable alias (default `"hub"`) not the real repo id; `matchTrustedMirror` resolves: (1) `state.json.pr_system.target_aliases`, (2) `git remote get-url origin` parsed to `org/repo`, (3) reject `unknown-target-repo-alias`. The wire carries only the alias; the real id stays operator-local (┬¦13.14).

#### 13.22.7 Authority + permission ŌĆö per-repo role mapping

An agent's role is a function of **(agent identity, target repo)**, not identity alone:

| Repo | EG agent role | `<hub-repo>` main agent role |
|------|---------------|------------------------------|
| EG (`SoliEstre/EstreGenesis`) | `main` | `peer/upstream` |
| `<hub-repo>` | `peer/upstream` | `main` |

The merge-authority gate is **strict**: only an agent with `role == main` *for the target repo* may emit `PRMergeRequest` (server `wsPrMergeReject`; non-main rejected + logged to `decisions`). Independent of provider ACL drift ŌĆö the protocol authority chain is deterministic. Load-bearing consequence: when EG (`main` for EG) issues `PRMergeRequest` against `<hub-repo>` (where EG is `peer/upstream`), the request is **rejected** ŌĆö merge authority on `<hub-repo>` rests with the `<hub-repo>` main-role agent. Other types follow the ┬¦13.22.3 server-filter column.

#### 13.22.8 State machine ŌĆö 5-state PR lifecycle (level-discriminated)

Both levels traverse the same logical states. **Level 2**: provider events (translated by the bridge into `PRStatusUpdate`) + review-authority emissions drive transitions; MERGED ŌēĪ `gh pr merge` succeeded. **Level 1**: A2A envelope events drive transitions (no provider state); `PRDraftReady` carries the staged commit SHA; `PRMergeRequest` triggers commit-to-integration-branch + push; MERGED ŌēĪ push succeeded (SHA reported in `PRMergeAck`).

```text
   PRRequest received ŌåÆ DRAFT ŌöĆŌöĆ(created [L2] / staged [L1])ŌöĆŌöĆŌåÆ OPEN ŌöĆŌöĆ(reviewer engages)ŌöĆŌöĆŌåÆ IN_REVIEW
                          Ōöé                                                                     Ōöé
                          ŌööŌöĆŌöĆ(rejected: invalid / unauthorized / capability mismatch)ŌöĆŌöĆŌåÆ CLOSED Ōöé
   IN_REVIEW ŌöĆŌöĆ(PRReviewAck approve)ŌöĆŌöĆŌåÆ APPROVED ŌöĆŌöĆ(PRMergeRequest [role==main] + PRMergeAck)ŌöĆŌöĆŌåÆ MERGED
   IN_REVIEW ŌöĆŌöĆ(PRReviewAck request-changes)ŌöĆŌöĆŌåÆ CHANGES_REQUESTED ŌöĆŌöĆ(requester follow-up)ŌöĆŌöĆŌåÆ IN_REVIEW (loop)
   (from any state ŌåÆ CLOSED: superseded or withdrawn)
```

**Composition with ┬¦13.19** ŌĆö a PR past SLA in `IN_REVIEW`/`CHANGES_REQUESTED` is a ┬¦13.19.2 quasi-deadlock candidate; the reviewer's `slaEta` on `request-changes` is a ┬¦13.19.7 `ReviewSLAAck`-shaped commitment; breach routes the ┬¦13.20 nudge ladder (polite ŌåÆ explicit ŌåÆ deadline ŌåÆ human), tier-4 escalates to the `decisions` panel with `class: 'pr-stalled'`. **Composition with ┬¦13.13** ŌĆö every emission gets server-auto `Ack{delivered}`; `AckProcessed` on request-parse + `PRDraftReady` on actual creation preserves the three-grade stratification. **Already-in-target cherry-pick skip (L1 merge handler)** ŌĆö in Level 1 the receiving bridge already committed the staged change to the target's local integration branch at apply time; on `PRMergeRequest`, check `git merge-base --is-ancestor <draftRef> <targetBranch>` BEFORE cherry-pick: if ancestor, skip cherry-pick ŌåÆ `git push` directly; else cherry-pick then push (avoids duplicate-commit). Level 2 unaffected (`gh pr merge` against a separate provider object).

#### 13.22.9 Cross-links

- **┬¦13.9** ŌĆö supplies the role model the ┬¦13.22.7 strict merge gate extends to per-repo dimensionality.
- **┬¦13.11** ŌĆö every PR-lifecycle emission is a board safe-point + MUST emit to the board (not bilateral-only); `PRStatusUpdate` is the periodic emission (same heartbeat-ban exception class as ┬¦13.19 / ┬¦13.20 ŌĆö fires on lifecycle events).
- **┬¦13.13** ŌĆö the substrate; every ┬¦13.22 emission gets server-auto `Ack{delivered}`; `PRDraftReady`/`PRReviewAck` compose with `AckProcessed`.
- **┬¦13.14** ŌĆö ┬¦13.22 follows redaction in its own text (`<hub-repo>` placeholder + `targetRepo` alias keep the production path off the wire); the ┬¦13.14/┬¦13.15 mirror PR is the *first artifact* ┬¦13.22 mirrors.
- **┬¦13.16.9** ŌĆö the five new `CUSTOM` types are subject to the A2A-intent allowlist; the ┬¦13.22.3 server-filter column is the per-type authority-gate extension.
- **┬¦13.17** ŌĆö `category: standard` `PRRequest` surfaces user-approval via the `decisions` panel, NOT inline `AskUserQuestion`; tier-4 PR-stalled escalations route the same way.
- **┬¦13.19** ŌĆö a PR past SLA in `IN_REVIEW` is a quasi-deadlock candidate; the ┬¦13.19.6 ladder applies on breach.
- **┬¦13.20** ŌĆö a PR-stalled blocker IS a ┬¦13.20 blocker; the nudge ladder applies, tier-4 carries `class: 'pr-stalled'`.

#### 13.22.10 Optional server-side PR observe tier (v2.4.16 ŌĆö board visibility, slightly above pure relay)

The base Constellation server treats `CUSTOM` as **pure relay** ŌĆö it routes without interpreting payloads (┬¦13.13 layer split). The PR system's five types are the one place a server MAY opt in to *slightly* more, and that excess must be declared, bounded, and opt-in:

- **(a) Observe set** ŌĆö the server watches the five ┬¦13.22.3 types as they relay and projects the PR lifecycle onto the board (per-PR card/panel tracking the ┬¦13.22.8 five-state machine). Observation is read-only over messages already in flight; it never alters, delays, or originates PR traffic.
- **(b) Merge-authority gate** ŌĆö `wsPrMergeReject`: a `PRMergeRequest` from any agent whose role is not `main` *for the target repo* is rejected and logged to the `decisions` panel. This is the server-side half of the ┬¦13.22.7 strict authority chain ŌĆö the one observe-tier behavior that is *more* than observation, justified because merge is the protocol's only irreversible transition.
- **(c) Strictly optional** ŌĆö the protocol is complete without this tier: Level 1 and Level 2 both function agent-side only. The tier adds visibility (a) and authority hardening (b); absence degrades neither correctness nor the lifecycle.
- **(d) Declared exception, no creep** ŌĆö when enabled, the server is content-aware for exactly these five types and nothing else. Register the tier as an explicit, named exception to the ┬¦13.13 layer split; extending content-awareness to any other `CUSTOM` family requires its own ┬¦-level case ŌĆö the PR tier is not a precedent for general payload inspection.
- **(e) Reference implementation** ŌĆö adopter-side (hub): a server `_PR_CUSTOM` observe set + `PRStatusUpdate` observation + the `wsPrMergeReject` strict gate, shipped additively alongside the local-bridge `createPR` port (dry-run default, live-PR env opt-in). EG ships this spec tier; the implementation stays adopter-side per the ┬¦13.22 provenance note.


**Provenance**: distilled from EG RRP `constellation/reference/docs/archive/2026-06-01-a2a-pr-system-rrp.md` into the adopted Phase 1 (Level 2 provider-mediated) + Phase 1b (Level 1 A2A-only) form, dogfood-validated by the ┬¦13.14/┬¦13.15 mirror as the first protocol-mediated PR (three structural defects ŌĆö `sourceContentRef.kind` placeholder lookup, missing `inline-section-mirror` handler, `targetPath` base ambiguity ŌĆö surfaced and resolved by the dry-run + review + `abs+exists` gate stack before any external publish). The PR-bot reference implementation lives adopter-side (local-bridge `createPR` port + server-side five-type observer + `wsPrMergeReject` strict gate); EG ships the protocol spec.

### 13.23 Backend registry + board-worker projection (C1)

#### 13.23.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.24 (2026-06-13). Absorbed from the `netwaif/multi-agent-starter` benchmark (MIT ŌĆö external-framework attribution per the EstreUX rule) as candidate **C1**, adjusted EG-native. The starter's `_shared/backends.json` is an **active call dispatcher** (`call_worker.sh` invokes models). EG is **turn-based** ŌĆö agents pick their own model at session start; the orchestrator never invokes them. So the same `role ŌåÆ model ŌåÆ connection` data is repurposed: **not a dispatcher but a declarative truth + verification + visualization surface**. Direct motivation: the 2026-06-11 board-observer model swap (SonnetŌåÆOpus) had to be tracked by memory alone ŌĆö who-is-which-model lived nowhere declarative. This section mechanizes that gap.

#### 13.23.2 The registry (`backends.json`)
- Schema: `{ board, agents: [{ agentId, role, model, connection, board }] }`.
- `role` Ōłł {`main`, `board-worker`, `local`, `upstream`, `collab`, `peer` (v2.4.52)} ┬Ę `connection` Ōłł {`bridge`, `local`, ŌĆ”} ┬Ę `board` Ōłł {`self`, `hub`, `self+hub`}.
- **Default location** = the Constellation coordination domain: reference example at `constellation/reference/dashboard/backends.json`; a deployment places its own instance wherever its coordination state lives (this maintenance workspace: `collab-self/backends.json`).
- **Re-sync preserve rule (v2.4.46)** ŌĆö `backends.json` is *deployment config, not runtime*. Because the reference example sits inside the `dashboard/` copy-set (and the dashboard's default fetch is the relative `./backends.json`), a wholesale vendor-copy re-sync clobbers the deployment's instance (board title, roster). Adapters keep `backends.json` on the re-sync **preserve-list** (or re-apply it after sync) ŌĆö surfaced by a downstream adapter's Migration-B full re-sync overwriting its branding.
- It is **declarative truth, not a dispatcher** ŌĆö turn-based agents are never invoked from it; it records what each agent *is*, for verification + projection. Absent file ŌåÆ graceful degradation everywhere (no board-worker split, no badges).

#### 13.23.3 board-worker is a projected role, not a wire role
The server role model (┬¦13.1) derives role from key-kind (collab/upstream) + `WS_PRIMARY_AGENT` (main), else `local`. Adding a `board-worker` *wire* role would require server + key-system changes. Instead board-worker is a **dashboard overlay**: the wire role stays `local`; the dashboard reads `backends.json` and re-classifies any agent declared `role: board-worker` into its own group. Fully decoupled ŌĆö zero server/protocol change. (The board-worker is the agent that maintains the live board ŌĆö done/current/planned/decisions ŌĆö on main's behalf.)

#### 13.23.4 Dashboard projection (board-worker tab group)
- A dedicated **board-worker group** sits between ļ®öņØĖ and ļĪ£ņ╗¼, containing **(a)** the board-worker channel tab and **(b)** a `­¤öĆ MainŌåöBoard` monitor ŌĆö the mainŌåöboard-worker A2A stream, split out of `­¤öĆ MainŌåöLocal` exactly as `­¤öĆ MainŌåöCollab` is split for collab peers (┬¦13.9 parallel).
- **Role/model badge** ŌĆö each agent tab carries its declared model (from `backends.json`) as a compact badge.
- **Color** ŌĆö board-worker inherits the former local hue (green `#39d353`); the generic local role moves to blue (`#4a9ed8`); the `--ws-role-*` SSoT is unified in the same cut. Deliberately **not amber** ŌĆö amber is reserved for Superscalar ┬¦4 Andon speculative lanes. Peer (v2.4.52) takes rose (`#d84a9e`).
- **Peer tab group (v2.4.52)** ŌĆö a dedicated **peer group** sits between ļĪ£ņ╗¼ and ĒśæņŚģ, containing **(a)** each attached peer-main's channel tab and **(b)** two monitors: `­¤öĆ PeerŌåöPeer` (A2A between attached peer-mains) and `­¤öĆ PeerŌåöCollab` (peer-main Ōåö collab traffic). The main group gains a third monitor `­¤öĆ MainŌåöPeer`, split out exactly as `­¤öĆ MainŌåöCollab` was. **Monitor classification is peer-first**: any A2A pair involving a `peer` endpoint classifies to the peer-family monitors (peer+peer ŌåÆ PeerŌåöPeer; peer+collab ŌåÆ PeerŌåöCollab; peer+anything-else ŌåÆ MainŌåöPeer) before the legacy upstream/collab/board precedence runs. All monitors ŌĆö the peer three and the legacy four alike ŌĆö are **lazily materialized**: a monitor tab renders only once its conversation has content (first A2A push creates the channel); an empty monitor never occupies tab space.
- **Prompt-target selector (v2.4.52)** ŌĆö the prompt-injection header row carries, at its right end, a compact selector that **always indicates the effective delivery target** (group-tinted dot + `optgroup`-per-group agent list). Selecting a tab or tab group immediately re-indicates the auto-resolved target (a group resolves to its representative worker); the operator MAY override the target for the current selection, and the override resets on the next tab/group switch. Monitor tabs stay read-only ŌĆö the selector disables rather than making a monitor writable.
- **Slash-command autocomplete (v2.4.67)** ŌĆö typing `/` at the start of the prompt-injection composer opens a candidate list that narrows as the token grows, mirroring a harness CLI palette: Ōåæ/Ōåō move the selection, Enter/Tab apply it (token completed + trailing space; Ctrl+Enter still sends as-is), **ESC closes the candidate list only** (never the window ŌĆö the keydown stops propagating so outer close handlers don't fire), and any whitespace ends the autocomplete session. Candidates are **manifest-first**: when the effective target (per the prompt-target selector) has declared a `CommandManifest`, its commands list first (ņäĀņ¢Ė-badged); targets without a declaration fall back to a deliberately conservative common set (Ļ│ĄĒåĄ-badged) whose descriptions state that interpretation belongs to the target harness ŌĆö the board never fabricates harness-specific palettes it cannot verify. Room targets get no candidates (room utterances are free speech, ┬¦13.30). Manifest values are wire-derived untrusted input ŌåÆ rendered textContent-only per ┬¦8.1. **Token-based trigger (v2.4.69)**: the autocomplete session opens wherever the token before the cursor ŌĆö the text after the last whitespace/newline ŌĆö matches `/` + command charset (`[A-Za-z0-9_-]`), so a command typed mid-sentence after a space or newline completes too; the moment the token stops looking like a command and starts looking like a path (a second `/`, a dot, any non-command character ŌĆö `src/foo`, `./x`, `/README.md`), the list closes itself. Apply replaces the token only, preserving surrounding text.
- **`CommandManifest` (v2.4.67, data-plane declaration)** ŌĆö an agent MAY declare the slash commands it can **actually honor when they arrive as prompt text**: `CUSTOM`/`CommandManifest` with `value.commands[{name, desc}]` (`name` must start with `/`; the server caps count and field lengths). The server keeps a per-agent latest-wins registry persisted beside the channel-role store (`ws-history/.cmd-manifests.json`) and ships it to boards inside the History payload (`manifests` field), so candidates survive refresh, cold channels, and history trimming. Because the declaration is an ordinary data-plane event ŌĆö not a bridge or protocol feature ŌĆö **any harness adapter declares its palette the same way** (Claude Code, Codex, Hermes, OpenClaw alike). Declaration rule: only commands the receiving agent can honor on receipt ŌĆö e.g. a Claude Code session declares its invocable skills, not host-CLI built-ins it cannot trigger itself; those generic verbs stay in the board-side fallback where their unverified nature is labeled.
- **Ops status strip + `OpsState` (v2.4.71)** ŌĆö the composer actions row carries, at its left end, a compact strip showing the effective target's operational state (`ŌÜÖ model┬Ęeffort┬Ęfast ┬Ę sub:on/off`); clicking opens a dropdown with the full breakdown. Data is declaration-first: a new `CUSTOM`/`OpsState` event (same class as `CommandManifest` ŌĆö **change-triggered declaration, not a periodic snapshot**; latest-wins; server-persisted at `ws-history/.ops-states.json` + shipped in the History payload's `opsStates` field) carries `{model?, effort?, fast?, subscaler?{on,pair,effort}, controls?[]}`, with the `backends.json` model as the undeclared fallback. Declaration rule mirrors the palette: **declare only measured truth** (a Claude Code session can measure its model and its subscaler marker, but not its per-request effort ŌĆö so it omits effort rather than guessing). Controls in the dropdown are honest the same way: an item is actionable **only when the target's `CommandManifest` declares the corresponding command** (e.g. `/subscaler` ŌĆö the click sends that text as a `UserPrompt`, the one path any harness honors); everything else renders read-only, because the board never fabricates a control path into a harness. Both declaration events are machine-consumed noise for humans: excluded from Web Push and from worker pending classifiers (the four-consumer filter discipline).

#### 13.23.5 verify-nway backend axis (static drift detection)
The EG-ops `verify-nway-version.cjs` gains a backend axis: **(1)** the reference `backends.json` is schema-valid; **(2)** every declared `role` is one the dashboard actually renders (the `byRole` set) ŌĆö a role nothing projects is drift; **(3)** where a deployment's instance + `local-keys/` both exist, every `connection: local` agent has a matching `local-keys/<id>.key` and every key file is declared ŌĆö the static proxy for "who is actually a local worker", catching the swap-tracking gap deterministically.

#### 13.23.6 Cross-links
┬¦13.1 role model ┬Ę ┬¦13.9 collab-peer monitor split (the parallel for MainŌåöBoard) ┬Ę Superscalar ┬¦4 Andon (amber reservation). Reference impl: `constellation/reference/dashboard/{app.js, style.css, backends.json}`; axis: EG-ops `verify-nway-version.cjs`.

### 13.24 PWA (installable + offline shell) + board title customization

#### 13.24.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.27 (2026-06-13). The reference dashboard becomes an installable PWA, and the board title becomes a per-deployment value (the EG self-board sets it to "EstreGenesis"). C2-adjacent UX absorption; dashboard-side, with one small server addition (MIME).

#### 13.24.2 PWA ŌĆö installable + offline shell (#3a)
- **`manifest.webmanifest`** ŌĆö standalone display, theme/background color, icons (192/512, `any` + `maskable`). The deployment supplies its own icon (this board uses the EstreGenesis symbol, square-padded 8% for the maskable safe zone).
- **`sw.js`** (service worker) ŌĆö app-shell **network-first** cache (dashboard updates land immediately; offline falls back to cache), live data (`/api`, `/ws`, `/join`) bypassed (never cached), `notificationclick` focuses the board window. Registered from `index.html`.
- **Server MIME** ŌĆö the static server's MIME map gains `.webmanifest` (`application/manifest+json`) + `.png`; a board restart applies it (manifest must serve with the correct type for install).
- **Notifications** ŌĆö **tier-1 shipped (v2.4.28)**: a ­¤öö settings dropdown (master toggle + per-item toggles ŌĆö Ļ▓ĆĒåĀņÜöņ▓Ł / A2A ņłśņŗĀ / ņ×æņŚģ ņśżļźś┬Ęņżæļŗ©) requests permission and fires `new Notification` on **live (non-replay)** events: a new unresolved decision (`renderDecisions` seen-set, first render suppressed), meaningful A2A (`a2acard` rows in `wsPushRow`), `RUN_ERROR`. Prefs persist to localStorage. **tier-2 shipped (v2.4.43 ŌĆö Web Push, ┬¦13.24.4)**: VAPID + server-held subscriptions, fires while the PWA is fully closed. This is the "human-gate ŌåÆ OS" surface (Superscalar agent-time vs human-time ŌĆö a notification shortens human-response latency).

#### 13.24.3 Board title customization (formal)
`backends.json` gains a **board-level `boardTitle`** field (default `"Constellation"`). At load the dashboard applies it to the topbar brand (`#board-name`) + the document title; `sync-dashboard` templates the *deployed* `manifest.webmanifest` `name`/`short_name` from it (so the PWA install name matches the deployment). Absent ŌåÆ `"Constellation"` default. EG self-board ŌåÆ `"EstreGenesis"`. This replaces the previously source-hardcoded title ŌĆö the board identity is now deployment config, not a fork point.

#### 13.24.4 tier-2 Web Push (#3b ŌĆö fires while the PWA is closed)
v2.4.43 (2026-06-20). tier-1 (┬¦13.24.2) only fires while a board tab/SW is alive; tier-2 closes that gap ŌĆö OS-level notifications delivered even when the dashboard is fully closed. Implemented **dependency-free** (node built-in `crypto`/`https` only ŌĆö no `web-push` library):
- **VAPID keypair** ŌĆö a P-256 (`prime256v1`) keypair self-generated via node `crypto`, persisted to `.vapid.json` (gitignored, per-deployment). The `applicationServerKey` handed to the browser is the uncompressed EC point (`0x04 || X || Y`, 65 bytes, base64url).
- **Signing** ŌĆö the VAPID JWT is ES256 (ECDSA P-256 + SHA-256); the JWS signature is the raw `r || s` 64-byte form via `crypto.sign(ŌĆ”, { dsaEncoding: 'ieee-p1363' })`. `aud` = push-endpoint origin, `exp` Ōēż 12h, `sub` = a `mailto:` contact.
- **tickle delivery** ŌĆö a payload-less VAPID push (RFC 8291 payload encryption is *avoided*, which is precisely what removes the library dependency). On the `push` event the service worker fetches `GET /api/push/latest` for the body and calls `showNotification`. Expired subscriptions (HTTP 404/410) are pruned automatically.
- **Endpoints** (4, on the UI surface ŌåÆ subject to the ┬¦13.25 `ui` allowlist): `GET /api/push/vapid-public-key`, `POST /api/push/subscribe`, `POST /api/push/unsubscribe`, `GET /api/push/latest`.
- **Trigger** ŌĆö every message crossing `wsToBoards` (the board-broadcast path that already carries A2A for dashboard observation) is filtered by a noise blocklist (Heartbeat / AgentList / Ack / OnboardAck / control kinds / non-CUSTOM run-and-stream frames); meaningful A2A intents (Report / Delegate / decision intents ŌĆ”) push. Title = `<agent> ┬Ę <intent>`, body = the message's `re` / `summary` / `text`.
- **Subscribe UX** ŌĆö the ­¤öö panel gains a **ļ░▒ĻĘĖļØ╝ņÜ┤ļō£ ņĢīļ”╝** toggle that requests permission, subscribes via `PushManager.subscribe({ userVisibleOnly: true, applicationServerKey })`, and POSTs the subscription; the toggle reflects the live subscription state.

Web Push is **per-origin**: each board origin holds its own VAPID keypair + subscriptions, so a board self-sufficiently pushes its own activity with no cross-origin dependency. Two boards sharing the same endpoint/key convention could later federate cross-board notifications.

### 13.25 Surface-scoped access control (#5a ŌĆö LAN-exposure allowlists)

#### 13.25.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.39 (2026-06-19). When the board is exposed beyond loopback (`WS_BIND` non-loopback ŌĆö the secure-by-default opt-in of v2.4.11), the three reachable surfaces gate **independently** rather than under one blanket rule. Purely additive ŌĆö with no `access.json` the runtime behaves exactly as before (all permitted; the v2.4.11 warning remains the only signal). The LAN bind itself is still the operator's explicit `WS_BIND` flip; this section governs only *who*, once bound, may reach *which* surface. **v2.4.41 (#5a-3)** extends it ŌĆö the **agent** surface gains its own IP allowlist (symmetric with UI/MCP), the `/ws` gating moves to HELLO (where agent vs MCP is known) with an upgrade-time pre-check to avoid leaking board state to fully-blocked IPs, `requireKey` is enforced at HELLO (URL *or* HELLO key ŌĆö fixing a v2.4.39 gap where only the URL key was seen), and allowlist entries accept **CIDR** ranges (`192.168.0.0/24`) as well as exact IPs. **v2.4.42 (#5a-4)** makes exposure dashboard-operable: a persisted **`expose`** field (the WS_BIND on/off) flipped via a loopback-only `POST /api/restart` that self-restarts the server (a deployment-provided `restart-self-board.ps1` re-launches it), with the settings-modal access editor surfaced as a distinct **save-gated block** (vs the real-time window-placement block).

#### 13.25.2 The three surfaces
One HTTP+WS port exposes three surfaces:
- **UI** ŌĆö the dashboard (`public/`) + the board endpoints (`/api/state`, `/api/events`, `/api/feedback`). Browser-reached, **no key** ŌåÆ gated by an IP allowlist.
- **agent** ŌĆö A2A WebSocket clients on `/ws`. Two independent layers: an **IP allowlist** (`agent.allowlist`, symmetric with UI/MCP) *and* an optional key requirement (`agent.requireKey`) that rejects unkeyed/invalid-key joins ŌĆö closing the v2.4.11 unauthenticated-board vector (anyone on the LAN issuing keys / `SetMain`). Defence-in-depth: "only my known IPs **and** only with a key".
- **MCP** ŌĆö the MCP-proxy WS client (┬¦8), identified at HELLO by `capabilities` containing `'mcp-proxy'` ŌåÆ its own IP allowlist, **independent of UI and agent** (e.g. expose the dashboard to LAN phones while keeping MCP loopback-only).

All three IP allowlists accept exact IPs (IPv4/IPv6) and IPv4 CIDR ranges (`a.b.c.d/n`).

`/join/*` onboarding + the integration-doc whitelist are agent-facing and already key-gated, so they are **exempt** from the UI allowlist (IP-blocking them would break remote agent onboarding).

#### 13.25.3 `access.json` (server-side, gitignored)
A file beside `server.cjs` (`ACCESS_FILE` env relocates it), hot-reloaded via `fs.watchFile` (no restart):
```json
{ "expose": false, "ui": { "allowlist": null }, "agent": { "allowlist": null, "requireKey": false }, "mcp": { "allowlist": null } }
```
- `allowlist`: `null`/absent = **allow-all** (default); an array = only those entries ŌĆö each an **exact IP** (IPv4/IPv6) or an **IPv4 CIDR** range (`a.b.c.d/n`; IPv6 CIDR not yet, exact IPv6 works). Loopback (`127.0.0.1` / `::1`, IPv4-mapped `::ffff:` normalized) is **always** allowed.
- `agent.requireKey`: when `true`, a `/ws` join from a non-loopback IP without a valid registered key (`wsValidKey`, resolved from the URL *or* the HELLO message) is closed at HELLO.
- `expose` (#5a-4): when `true`, the server binds `0.0.0.0` (LAN) instead of `127.0.0.1` **if the `WS_BIND` env is unset** (env always wins). A **bind-time** value ŌĆö changing it takes effect only on restart (`/api/restart`), unlike the allowlists which hot-reload.
- **Fail-open by default**: a missing/corrupt file resets to the all-permissive default (incl. `expose:false`) ŌĆö a security gate is an explicit opt-in, never an accidental lockout. On a loopback bind the IP gate is wholly inert (a local-only board needs no IP rules).

#### 13.25.4 Enforcement points
- **UI** ŌĆö top of the HTTP handler, before routing (exempting `/join/*` + integration docs): non-allowed IP ŌåÆ `403`.
- **`/ws` upgrade pre-check** ŌĆö agent and MCP share the `/ws` transport and are only distinguished at HELLO, yet the server emits board state (AgentList/History) right after the handshake. So at `upgrade`, an exposed-non-loopback IP blocked on **both** `agent` and `mcp` is `socket.destroy()`'d before any state is sent (leak prevention); an IP allowed on either passes through to HELLO.
- **agent / MCP** ŌĆö at `HELLO` the surface is resolved (`mcp-proxy` capability ŌåÆ `mcp`, else `agent`) and that surface's IP allowlist is applied; then, if `requireKey`, the key (URL or HELLO) is checked. Either failure ŌåÆ `conn.close()` before the agent registers.

#### 13.25.5 `/api/access`
- `GET /api/access` ŌåÆ `{ ok, access, exposed, bind }` (behind the UI gate ŌĆö only UI-allowed callers read it).
- `POST /api/access` ŌåÆ replaces the config (shape-validated, then `loadAccess()`). **Loopback-only** ŌĆö the operator manages allowlists from the local machine; a remote caller (even a UI-allowed one) cannot rewrite the access policy.
- `POST /api/restart` (#5a-4) ŌåÆ **loopback-only** self-restart, to apply an `expose` change: spawns the deployment's `restart-self-board.ps1` (Windows: via `cmd /c start` for a true detach that survives the server's own exit ŌĆö a plain detached spawn does not) then `process.exit`s; the script frees the port and re-launches `start-self-board.ps1`, the new process reading the new `expose`. Absent script / non-Windows ŌåÆ logged no-op (manual restart).

#### 13.25.6 Cross-links
- v2.4.11 secure-by-default bind ŌĆö the opt-in this section refines.
- ┬¦3.1 KEY-MGMT ŌĆö the keys the `agent` surface trusts.
- ┬¦8 MCP integration ŌĆö the `mcp-proxy` client this gates.
- The dashboard access editor (settings-modal "ņĀæņåŹ ņĀ£ņ¢┤" section ŌĆö a distinct **save-gated block** vs the real-time ņ░Į ļ░░ņ╣ś block): a **ļäżĒŖĖņøīĒü¼ ļģĖņČ£ ļüäĻĖ░/ņ╝£ĻĖ░** master toggle (`expose`; dims the IP policy when off), per-surface **ĻĖ░ļ│Ė ņ░©ļŗ©/ĒŚłņÜ®** toggles for UI/agent/MCP each with a CIDR-capable allowlist textarea, a `requireKey` checkbox, an exposed/bind status badge, and an exposed-without-key warning. **ņĀĆņ×ź** writes `access.json` (allowlists hot-reload); **ņĀĆņ×ź ļ░Å ņ×¼ņŗ£ņ×æ** also `POST /api/restart`s to apply an `expose` change. Shipped v2.4.40 (#5a-2) ŌåÆ 3 surfaces + CIDR v2.4.41 (#5a-3) ŌåÆ expose toggle + self-restart + block separation v2.4.42 (#5a-4). Settings modal title generalized to "ŌÜÖ ņäżņĀĢ".

#### 13.25.7 Multi-hat operator ŌĆö hub operator = peer (small-team identity, v2.4.48)

In a small team the same human (and their agent) is often **both** the hub operator and a peer ŌĆö e.g. the operator who runs the NAS hub over SSH is also an `upstream` peer on it. "Who issues the key, to whom" then converges on oneself, and the legitimacy of self-issuance was undefined.

- **Per-role-instance canonical-id (MUST)**: even under one operating human, the `hub-main` role (e.g. `nas-hub-main`) and the `peer-main` role (e.g. `estre-peer`) take **separate** canonical ids ŌĆö they are distinct roles, not aliases, so the ┬¦13.9.2 alias-collapsing discipline does NOT apply to them.
- **Self-issuance is legitimate**: in an operator-is-peer deployment, self-issuing a `uk-` key is a normal procedure, not a smell. Record the issuance in board history or the backup repo (┬¦13.28) for auditability (SHOULD).
- **The real trust boundary is the surface allowlist (┬¦13.25) + the secret-storage location, not the key ceremony.** A small team SHOULD NOT defer adoption over key procedure ŌĆö starting with `requireKey=false` on a loopback / LAN-trusted board is a valid posture; add keys when the exposure surface grows.

### 13.26 Echo-mode ŌĆö mirroring an agent's local chat to the board (remote-control substrate)

An agent's *primary* interface is its own client (Claude Code, an IDE, a terminal) where a human converses with it directly. The board, by contrast, is a *shared observation + coordination* surface. **Echo-mode** bridges the two: when an agent's echo-mode is ON, its local humanŌåöagent conversation is mirrored **bidirectionally** onto the board's real-time conversation channel, so a human watching the board can both *see* and *drive* that agent through the board. This turns Constellation into a **remote-control** surface for the agents on it.

Echo-mode is a per-agent mode, not a board-wide setting. It reuses the existing real-time conversation wire (┬¦13.16.12) and dashboard rendering ŌĆö it adds a *protocol discipline*, not a new transport. It has **three levels** (┬¦13.26.4): **off**, **on** (turn-final conversation), and **mirror** (a live activity stream that also echoes progress and thinking, at the level of a chat-gateway bot).

#### 13.26.1 The two directions

- **Local ŌåÆ board (outbound mirror).** While echo-mode is enabled the agent mirrors onto its own board channel ŌĆö *what* is mirrored depends on the **level** (┬¦13.26.4):
  - the **human's local prompt** that opened the turn ŌåÆ a `UserPrompt` with `source:'user'` (both levels; so the board shows *both* sides of the conversation). *(A prompt that arrived **from** the board is already on the board ŌĆö do not re-emit it; just quote it locally per the inbound rule below.)*
  - each **assistant turn's output** ŌåÆ a `TEXT_MESSAGE` (streaming `TEXT_MESSAGE_START`/`_CONTENT`/`_END` when available, else one complete `TEXT_MESSAGE`) ŌĆö **both levels**.
  - **`mirror` level only** ŌĆö a live activity stream *as the turn runs*: tool calls ŌåÆ `TOOL_CALL_START`/`_ARGS`/`_END`/`_RESULT` cards, step boundaries ŌåÆ `STEP_STARTED`/`_FINISHED`, run boundaries ŌåÆ `RUN_STARTED`/`_FINISHED`, and **thinking narration** ŌåÆ short `TEXT_MESSAGE`/`STEP` status lines ("analyzing XŌĆ”", a turn-end thinking summary). Raw chain-of-thought is not streamed verbatim (too verbose, and no host thinking-hook exists); the mirror level emits *progress + narration + summary*, which is the chat-gateway (e.g. Telegram-bot) echo level.
- **Board ŌåÆ local (inbound drive).** A human typing into the board's real-time window for this agent emits a `UserPrompt` (dashboard `wsSend`, ┬¦13.16.12) that reaches the agent's inbox (┬¦13.16). On receipt the agent **MUST first echo the received prompt back into its local chat as a quoted line** (`> board: <text>`) and *then* act on it ŌĆö so the local transcript stays a faithful, self-contained record even when the driving input arrived out-of-band. Inbound drive works at every enabled level (`on` and `mirror`).

#### 13.26.2 Structured-choice reconciliation (the ┬¦13.17 tension)

┬¦13.17 forbids blocking structured-choice prompts in the main chat (they must route to the board). Echo-mode makes this a hard constraint rather than a guideline, because a blocking selection UI in the local chat would **hold the turn** and defeat remote-control (the human at the board could never advance it). Therefore, while echo-mode is ON, an agent facing a decision:

1. In the **local chat**, renders the options as **plain text** (`1/2/3` or `a/b/c` + a one-line each) and accepts a **free-form prompt** ŌĆö never a blocking selection widget. The turn does not hold on a local UI.
2. On the **board**, emits a `SelectionPrompt` (┬¦13.16.12 #406 UI6) so the real-time window shows the rich chip-card UI.
3. Resolves on **either** path: a board answer (`SelectionAnswer` ŌåÆ `SelectionResolved`) *or* the human typing the option token as a local/board `UserPrompt`. First resolution wins; the other surface is dimmed (`SelectionResolved`).

This is the same "one decision, two faithful surfaces" property as ┬¦13.17, generalized to the echo-mirror.

#### 13.26.3 Default by provenance (who joined whom)

Echo-mode's value is *giving a human a channel to an agent they otherwise cannot reach*. So the default follows **join provenance**:

| How the agent joined | Default echo-mode | Why |
|---|:-:|---|
| **Human-joined** (a person issued its key / started it) | **OFF** | The human already has a direct channel (that agent's own client). Mirroring is redundant and noisy ŌĆö opt in only when remote-control is wanted. |
| **Agent-spawned** (another agent called/spawned it ŌĆö e.g. a board-observer via `join-local.cjs`, a sub-worker) | **ON** | The human has **no** direct client for this agent; the board is the *only* place they can see or drive it. Echo-mode makes it reachable. |

The default is **per-agent overridable** by the user (`/echo-mode on|off <agentId>`), and a human-issued explicit instruction always wins over the provenance default.

#### 13.26.4 Levels + toggle

Echo-mode is a **three-level** per-agent setting:

| Level | Mirrors (local ŌåÆ board) | Use |
|---|---|---|
| **off** | nothing | Default for human-joined agents (┬¦13.26.3). |
| **on** | the human's prompt + the assistant's **turn-final text** + selection prompts | Conversation echo ŌĆö a human at the board sees the exchange and can drive it, without the tool-by-tool noise. |
| **mirror** | everything in `on` **+ live progress** (tool calls, steps, run boundaries) **+ thinking narration/summary**, streamed *as the turn runs* | Chat-gateway-level echo (Telegram-bot feel) ŌĆö the board shows *what the agent is doing right now*, not just the final answer. |

- **`/echo-mode off|on|mirror|status [agentId]`** (skill, ┬¦13.26.6) is the control surface. With no `agentId` it targets the invoking agent; with one it targets that agent (main-authority gated, like other cross-agent controls). BoardŌåÆlocal *inbound drive* works at both `on` and `mirror`; only the *outbound* richness differs.
- **State** is a per-agent level the agent reads to decide what to mirror, and announces to the board so the dashboard can badge the agent and treat its channel as a live conversation. Reference: a local `.echo-mode` marker keyed by `agentId` (`{ level, provenance }`) for the agent's own runtime + an `EchoModeState { agentId, level, provenance }` CUSTOM announced on change (idempotent; the board badges the agent and, when enabled, renders its channel as the primary conversation rather than a monitor lane).

#### 13.26.5 Granularity by level + exposure (honest constraints)

- **Granularity is per level, and neither level is token-streaming.** `on` is **turn-granular**: the board receives the agent's *complete* turn text at turn-end (one `TEXT_MESSAGE`), via the Stop hook. `mirror` is **action-granular**: tool calls and steps stream to the board *as they happen* (PostToolUse hook, one emit per tool call) so the board tracks live progress ŌĆö but the text *within* a single message is still not streamed keystroke-by-keystroke (no host token-streaming hook exists). An agent that *can* stream natively MAY use `TEXT_MESSAGE_START/_CONTENT/_END` for a finer feel.
- **Exposure is disclosure.** Echo-mode copies the local chat onto the board, so the board's access surface (┬¦13.25 #5a) governs *who* can now read that conversation. Mirroring to a network-exposed board is a disclosure event ŌĆö echo-mode MUST respect ┬¦13.14 redaction on what it emits, and SHOULD warn (or refuse) when the target board is exposed beyond loopback/allowlist. Remote-control convenience never overrides the access gate.

#### 13.26.6 Mechanization (reference) + cross-links

- **Reference emit ŌĆö level-tiered hooks.** `echo-emit.cjs` reads the agent's `.echo-mode` level (keyed by `agentId`) and emits accordingly:
  - **`on`** ŌĆö a **Stop** hook extracts the last assistant turn from the session transcript and emits it as `TEXT_MESSAGE` on the agent's board channel; a local opening prompt ŌåÆ `UserPrompt{source:'user'}`.
  - **`mirror`** ŌĆö additionally a **PostToolUse** hook emits each tool call as `TOOL_CALL_*` cards *as it completes* (live progress); a **PreToolUse** hook MAY emit a `STEP`/status line ("running XŌĆ”"); the Stop hook also appends a short **thinking summary** distilled from the turn's thinking blocks; `RUN_STARTED`/`_FINISHED` bracket the turn.
  - All emit hooks are **level-gated**: no-op at `off`, and the `mirror`-only tiers (PreToolUse/PostToolUse, thinking summary) are skipped at `on`.
- **Emit formatting (board-legibility).** Mirrored text lands in the board's conversation stream, so format for that target: put **sequenced/numbered items each on their own line** (one `ŌæĀ`/`1.` item per line, never an inline run-on), and prefer short lines. A render-target formatting rule, not a content rule.
- **Provenance default + state announce (reference, v2.4.58).** `join-local.cjs` ŌĆö the agent-spawned join path ŌĆö seeds the `.echo-mode` marker with `{ level:'on', provenance:'agent-spawned' }` when the joining agent has no entry, and never overwrites an existing entry (explicit toggles included ŌĆö ┬¦13.26.3's explicit-wins rule mechanized). On every (re)connect it (re)announces `EchoModeState` as an untargeted broadcast (idempotent; not a commitment-ack target, so no redelivery noise). The reference dashboard consumes the announce as a per-tab echo badge (`on` plain / `mirror` highlighted) ŌĆö the "board badges the agent" half of ┬¦13.26.4.
- **Workflow-run mirror + floating inspector (reference, v2.4.61).** A deployment MAY run a watcher that mirrors multi-agent workflow runs onto the agent's channel: coalesced `STEP_*` lines (­¤¦Ą-prefixed, one per poll tick at most) carrying a `wfRunId` field, plus a `WorkflowStatus` CUSTOM snapshot (`{runId, name, status, started, done, phases[], agents[{id, label?, state, preview?}], totalTokens?, durationMs?, logsTail?}`, throttled Ōēź10s per run). The reference dashboard consumes both: ­¤¦Ą STEP rows become clickable and open a **floating inspector** (draggable header, horizontal resize, content-height body, collapse + close) that live-renders the latest snapshot; history replay re-hydrates it, so completed runs stay inspectable. v2.4.63 widens the inspector into an **agent-activity monitor**: a second `SubagentStatus` snapshot (`{agents[{id, lastActivityS, sizeKB, state}], count}` ŌĆö standalone subagent transcripts active within a 10-minute window, chosen because a measured agent composing one large tool call went 6+ minutes without a transcript flush) renders as its own section, a fixed ­¤¦Ą fab toggles the layer without needing a STEP row, and the window styles from the dashboard's real theme tokens so it follows light/dark mode (the v2.4.61 styling had pinned itself to dark fallbacks of nonexistent variables). Measured constraint that shaped the design: the harness's run-state file is a completion-time artifact ŌĆö live progress must come from the run's journal, with the state file as the terminal enrichment (labels, tokens, duration).
- **Mirror-watcher operational contract (v2.4.73).** The watcher process itself carries duties the event contract above doesn't state: **(a) single-instance** ŌĆö a PID lock refuses duplicate watchers (two watchers double every card); **(b) no restart replay** ŌĆö a durable per-run cursor records what was already announced, and a run first discovered *already terminal* registers silently (a watcher restart must not re-announce history); **(c) per-tick coalescing** ŌĆö at most one progress line per run per poll tick regardless of how many journal events landed (fan-out workflows otherwise flood the channel); **(d) echo-gated at the source** ŌĆö the watcher reads the agent's `.echo-mode` level every tick and emits nothing at `off`: the mirror is part of the agent's echo surface, not an independent channel; **(e) identity fallback** ŌĆö live journals don't carry run names or phase lists, so the watcher resolves both from the run's script artifact (filename + meta block), degrading to the raw run id when absent; **(f) snapshot cadence** ŌĆö `WorkflowStatus` throttled Ōēź10 s per run, `SubagentStatus` on a heartbeat only while activity falls inside the 10-minute window, and both remain inside the machine-consumed noise classes (the ┬¦13.23.4 four-consumer filter discipline). Distilled from a measured deployment watcher (~180 lines, deps-0); the contract, not the script, is the portable part.
- **Behavioral fallback**: absent the hooks, the `/echo-mode` skill defines the same protocol as an agent behavior (emit turn output + progress + quote board prompts explicitly) ŌĆö the skill is the SSoT for the discipline; the hooks are the mechanization.
- **Cross-links**: ┬¦13.17 (main-chat structured-choice ŌåÆ board; echo-mode is its remote-control generalization) ┬Ę ┬¦13.16 / ┬¦13.16.12 (inbox + dashboard conversation render this reuses) ┬Ę ┬¦13.16.12 #406 UI6 `SelectionPrompt` (the choice UI) ┬Ę ┬¦13.25 #5a (access surface governing the mirror's audience) ┬Ę ┬¦13.14 (redaction on emitted content).

### 13.27 Headless hub-main ŌĆö autonomous reasoning loop (no human session)

#### 13.27.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.48 (2026-07-09). Distilled from a downstream-adapter dogfood (a NAS headless container curating a multi-project board, verified end-to-end). ┬¦4 runtime patterns assume a human session behind a turn-based agent; ┬¦3's autopilot is an in-session mode. **A board main that resides with no human session at all** ŌĆö the `hub-main` duty profile of ┬¦13.9.3 ŌĆö had no pattern in the spec or the reference runtime. This section is the pattern; the reference scripts are upstream candidates (┬¦13.27.3).

#### 13.27.2 Invariants
A headless hub-main is a **supervisor loop** that spawns a one-shot reasoning process (a `claude -p`-style headless invocation) per wake. The loop MUST satisfy:

1. **Wake economy (event-driven MUST)** ŌĆö the loop reasons only on an inbox change that passes the ┬¦13.16.9 meaningful filter (the A2A-intent group). Idle-heartbeat reasoning is forbidden (the loop form of the no-idle-chatter rule). A watcher blocks until a meaningful change (reference: `self-wake-watcher.sh` with `WS_STANDBY_MODE=always`, ┬¦13.16.6).
2. **Cursor discipline (at-least-once MUST)** ŌĆö a reasoning turn that fails (abnormal exit / timeout) MUST NOT advance the inbox cursor; the next wake idempotently re-processes the same span. The cursor advances **only on success**. This extends ┬¦13.13.2's receiver-side at-least-once up into the agent (reasoning) layer.
3. **Noise absorption (SHOULD)** ŌĆö if every new line is in a noise group, advance the cursor without spawning a reasoning process (a second check downstream of the watcher filter ŌĆö defence against filter drift).
4. **Security boundary (SHOULD)** ŌĆö the reasoning process runs in a cwd from which secret directories are unreachable, with a minimal tool allowlist (file R/W only, no shell). The board + doc stores are the only explicitly-granted extra paths.
5. **Turn timeout (MUST)** ŌĆö a wall-clock ceiling per turn (reference value 900s); on hang the supervisor reclaims the process.
6. **Model routing (┬¦13.16.9 `tier` consumer)** ŌĆö because each wake is a separate process, the `tier`ŌåÆmodel+effort mapping is free: a hub-main SHOULD route `routine` intents to a low-cost model / low effort and `escalation` intents to a high-capability model / high effort. Grounding (dogfood): bookkeeping is intelligence-insensitive, and for a resident agent the token/quota economy is the dominant variable.

#### 13.27.3 Reference runtime ŌĆö `constellation/reference/runtime/hub-main/` (v2.4.49, upstreamed)
The adopter's verified implementation was contributed under ┬¦13.14 redaction and now ships in-repo at **`constellation/reference/runtime/hub-main/`** (generalization substitution points in its README):
- `hub-loop.sh` ŌĆö supervisor: watcher(block, `WS_STANDBY_MODE=always`) ŌåÆ turn ŌåÆ backup, looping; echoes dependency paths at startup; initializes the cursor to the current line count on first start (no past-noise re-processing).
- `hub-turn.sh` ŌĆö ŌæĀ pull the doc repo (best-effort, `GIT_ASKPASS`) ŌåÆ ŌæĪ classify inbox-since-cursor in one node pass (noise absorb / `tier` decide ŌĆö the lists mirror the ┬¦13.16.9 4-group + tier SSoT, lockstep-updated; unclassified non-noise fail-safes to `escalation`) ŌåÆ Ōæó `tier`ŌåÆmodel+effort one-shot with a minimal tool allowlist + `add-dir` + 900s timeout ŌåÆ ŌæŻ advance the cursor **only on success**.
- `hub-backup.sh` ŌĆö on change: add ŌåÆ secret gate (┬¦13.28.3) ŌåÆ commit ŌåÆ push; a push failure keeps the local commit and retries next tick (offline tolerance).

Companion artifacts (same directory): `git-askpass.sh` (┬¦13.28.5 headless git auth), `Dockerfile` baking stable deps (restart tolerance), and the hub-main charter `CLAUDE.md.template` (┬¦13.9.3). The loop reuses the parent `runtime/self-wake-watcher.sh` as its blocking watcher.

#### 13.27.4 The loop contract ŌĆö implementation-independent statement (v2.4.56)
┬¦13.27.2's invariants were written against one runtime shape (`claude -p` one-shots under a bash supervisor). Restated as an **implementation-independent contract**, so any runtime that owns its own agent loop ŌĆö a local-LLM personal-AI environment, a provider-native scheduler, an embedded worker ŌĆö can be a conforming EG loop without resembling the reference scripts. A conforming loop provides **five elements**:

1. **Wake sources** ŌĆö a declared, enumerable set of change feeds (inbox file, WS push, queue) with a meaningful-filter at the boundary (┬¦13.16.9 SSoT). No polling-as-reasoning; no idle wakes. *Room traffic composes here*: ┬¦13.30 room messages wake a worker-class participant only on `Delegate` or explicit `addressee` naming (the D1 silence default, enforced at the filter ŌĆö dogfood-measured 2026-07-18).
2. **At-least-once consumption** ŌĆö a durable cursor per feed; advance **only on turn success**; failed turns re-process idempotently. Consumers therefore MUST be id-idempotent (the charter carries this duty).
3. **A charter** ŌĆö the per-wake process receives a written role contract (scope, autonomy boundary, file contracts, reply obligations, machine-count rules). The charter is an artifact, versioned with the deployment ŌĆö never implicit prompt memory.
4. **Model routing** ŌĆö the `tier`ŌåÆmodel+effort mapping of ┬¦13.27.2-6, generalized: the loop MAY route each wake to any model the operator owns (including local models); the contract only requires that `escalation`-tier intents never route below the deployment's declared capability floor.
5. **Safety boundary** ŌĆö per-wake tool/path allowlists + wall-clock ceiling + supervisor reclaim. The loop, not the model, owns termination.

Standing idle duty (v2.4.59): a resident loop that owns a board SHOULD spend idle capacity on the ┬¦13.31.4-Ōæź sweep cadence ŌĆö when board-update traffic has been silent for the idle window while work signals continue, the next tick runs the retrospective sweep (the boardsweep skill) instead of sleeping.

Conformance today: the reference `hub-main/` scripts (┬¦13.27.3) and the EG-ops `observer-loop`/`observer-turn` pair are the two measured implementations; a ┬¦13.30-aware wake filter is part of both since 2026-07-18. Composition: a host that implements this contract *and* the kit's Harness Adapter Contract (`plugins/HARNESS-ADAPTER-CONTRACT.md`, Stage 3) runs EG disciplines unattended on its own loop ŌĆö the two contracts deliberately partition "when the agent runs" (here) from "what it runs with" (adapter).

#### 13.27.5 Turn-spawned local worker ŌĆö the worker profile of the loop contract (v2.4.72)

The hub-main shape (┬¦13.27.2-.3) keeps a reasoning presence resident. A **local worker** (a board scribe, a delegation executor ŌĆö ┬¦13.23's projected role) inverts the economics: the *model* should exist only while there is work. The worker profile is the loop contract's five elements plus the worker-specific commitments a month of measured operation surfaced:

1. **Supervisor / turn split** ŌĆö a tiny deterministic **supervisor** stays resident (bridge liveness, wake detection per element 1, spawn, wall-clock reclaim); each wake spawns a **stateless one-shot turn process** whose prompt carries the charter *and the inbound to process, attached verbatim* ŌĆö the turn never discovers work, it receives it. No model runs between wakes.
2. **Charter commitments (worker additions to element 3)** ŌĆö the worker charter states: turn scope is *attached inbound + reply, nothing else* (no exploration, no opportunistic refactoring); an **autonomy split** (registrations and record updates autonomous; decisions, brief-writing, and loss/external-publish actions re-delegated **upward** ŌĆö the worker asks the main, never improvises); the board's canonical entry schema **embedded in the charter** (a charter without the schema is how a consumer-contract mismatch stays undiscoverable, ┬¦13.31.4-ŌæŻ); and a **machine-count rule** ŌĆö any count the worker reports (array lengths, totals) comes from executing a command, never from estimation (three measured miscounts before this rule).
3. **Id-idempotency as the at-least-once dual (element 2 made concrete)** ŌĆö the delivery layer redelivers; therefore every registration checks the target id before writing (present ŌåÆ skip, reported as an idempotent-skip), every removal tolerates an already-absent target, and duplicates are never created. A worker that is not idempotent turns the transport's safety property into data corruption.
4. **Session reuse with rotation (SHOULD; candidate sixth element of ┬¦13.27.4)** ŌĆö one-shot turns pay a cold-context tax per wake. A conforming worker MAY resume a fixed session across turns (warm context), provided it **rotates** the session on charter change (hash the charter into the session key) or after N turns, and self-cleans retired session artifacts. Measured effect: a stale un-rotated session is the charter-drift vector, and unbounded session files are the disk-drift vector ŌĆö rotation caps both. Promoted here as the worker profile's own commitment; flagged as a candidate sixth element for the general loop contract once a second implementation measures it.
5. **Silence is a valid output** ŌĆö noise-class traffic (room messages without delegation or explicit addressee, snapshot events, feedback passthrough) produces **no reply at all**: a per-message "cannot process" report is itself noise (dogfood-measured ŌĆö skip-reports flooded the very channel the filter existed to quiet). The reply contract is one report **per delegation**, not per message; user-authored feedback is notified upward untouched, never filtered or judged by the worker.
6. **Escalation on repeated failure** ŌĆö the supervisor counts consecutive failed turns and escalates to the main agent past a threshold; silent infinite retry is forbidden (the turn's failure report and the supervisor's escalation are different layers ŌĆö both required).
7. **Completion truth is state, not acknowledgment** ŌĆö transport acks (`delivered`, `delivered-persist` ŌĆö ┬¦13.13.2) are emitted by bridges on their own authority and prove nothing about worker processing (measured: clean acks throughout a multi-day worker outage). The delegator judges completion **only by reading the state the worker was asked to change**; worker-reported counts are trusted only when machine-generated (commitment 2).

The EG-ops `observer-loop`/`observer-turn` pair is the measured reference of this profile (supervisor ~80 lines, turn wrapper ~240, charter as a versioned markdown artifact); generalized reference scripts are an upstream candidate on the ┬¦13.27.3 pattern once a second deployment needs them.

### 13.28 Board persistence & backup contract

#### 13.28.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.48 (2026-07-09, downstream-adapter dogfood). The board `state.json` is the SSoT, yet lives as a single file on a single machine, and the spec had no durable-backup contract (┬¦13.25.3 only notes `access.json` is gitignored). Version-controlling the deployment directory is the natural backup ŌĆö but doing it naively staged secrets. This section is the contract that makes board backup safe.

#### 13.28.2 Tracked vs transient classification
- **tracked** ŌĆö `state.json` ┬Ę runtime code ┬Ę dashboard static assets ┬Ę (with care) `access.json` *only if it carries no key material*.
- **transient (MUST NOT track)** ŌĆö the transport queues (`inbox` / `outbox` / `feedback`), cursors, locks, `ws-history/`, logs, the agent-credential cache `HOME`, and binary-prefixed files. **Tracking a transport queue permanently records A2A message bodies** ŌĆö a secret / PII exposure surface, so transient is MUST here.

#### 13.28.3 Secret gate (MUST)
Before each commit, scan the staged content for real-token structural patterns and, on a hit, unstage + abort the push. Patterns are tightened to **real-token structure** so the gate script's own pattern literals do not self-match (observed failure: a gate whose literal `sk-ant-oat` string matched itself ŌåÆ a backup ABORT loop): e.g. `sk-ant-oat01-[A-Za-z0-9_-]{20,}`, `ghp_[A-Za-z0-9]{20,}`, `-----BEGIN [A-Z ]*PRIVATE KEY-----`. Tightening beats excluding the gate from tracking ŌĆö the gate itself is worth versioning.

#### 13.28.4 `.gitignore` contract
Comments on their **own line only** (git parses a trailing/inline comment as part of the pattern) and **LF-enforced** (CRLF turns every pattern into `pattern\r`, silently disabling all matching ŌåÆ secret staging; the two real incidents behind this section). Ship a reference `.gitignore` + a `.gitattributes` (scripts `eol=lf`; cf. `constellation/reference/runtime/.gitattributes`).

#### 13.28.5 Backup trigger + headless auth
The hub-main loop's turn-end hook (or a state-write hook) drives the backup; the commit message carries a snapshot timestamp; a push failure keeps the local commit and retries next tick (offline tolerance). Headless git auth SHOULD use a `GIT_ASKPASS` helper that references the PAT from env only (no plaintext credential file on disk ŌĆö important when `HOME` sits inside the backed-up directory): the helper file itself is not a secret and is trackable, unlike `credential.helper store`'s plaintext output.

### 13.29 Ownership registry & claim layering (conflict prevention)

#### 13.29.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.48 (2026-07-09, downstream-adapter dogfood). ┬¦13.19 (deadlock) / ┬¦13.20 (blocker) / ┬¦13.22 (cross-repo PR) are *post-conflict* protocols. In multi-repo orchestration (an overview doc repo + N code repos + per-peer ownership splits) the actual first line of defence against conflict was a **static ownership registry** (the adopter's `AGENTS.md` ownership table). The protocol did not know about it, so a hub-main had no board data to detect "two peers reporting the same unit."

#### 13.29.2 Registry contract
The board `state.json` gains an optional `ownership: [{ unit, owner (canonical-id), repo?, note? }]` field ŌĆö the hub-main mirrors the owning doc's ownership table (the SSoT is the doc; the board field is a **projection**). This makes ownership comparable against the `unit` field of a peer's `WorkerReport` (the ┬¦13.16.9 recommended payload, added same cut).

#### 13.29.3 Claim layering (3 layers)
ŌæĀ **static ownership** (registry ŌĆö the default boundary) ŌåÆ ŌæĪ **durable claim** (a git file, for cross-cutting files ŌĆö valid even offline) ŌåÆ Ōæó **live claim** (A2A `HandoffRequested` / `Handoff` ŌĆö immediate cross-session coordination). Rule: *a lower layer's claim MUST NOT contradict a higher layer; cross-unit work takes ŌæĪ first and notifies via Ōæó.*

#### 13.29.4 Violation surfacing (SHOULD)
A hub-main (coordination duty) that detects an out-of-ownership report by registry comparison SHOULD surface it on the `decisions` track ŌĆö **not** auto-block (the ownership table itself may be provisional; a human adjudicates).

#### 13.29.5 Contract-transition intent (candidate)
A new A2A intent under evaluation ŌĆö `ContractUpdate { contract, from, to, refs }` (tier `escalation`) ŌĆö to announce an interface-contract (`_contracts`-class) DRAFT ŌåÆ REVIEW ŌåÆ ACTIVE transition. It becomes the trigger signal for N-way surface sync when one feature spans multiple repo surfaces.

### 13.30 Roundtable ŌĆö multi-party topic rooms (3+ participants)

#### 13.30.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.53 (2026-07-17). Everything before this section is 1:1 ŌĆö a targeted message, one sender, one receiver. That shape does not scale to three or more speakers: a two-agent messenger-group dogfood produced an **echo storm** (both agents answering every human message, then answering each other's answers), the same announcement had to be delivered N times over N 1:1 channels, and per-pair threads fragmented the shared context so that one side went stale without knowing. A 5-axis deep research pass (121 sources, 12 adversarially verified claims) converged on one structure across frameworks, chat-protocol standards, and incident history: a **two-layer split** ŌĆö deterministic floor control belongs to the protocol, probabilistic speech judgment belongs to agent discipline. LLMs are measurably weaker at *when to speak* than at *what to say*, so every surveyed framework pairs model judgment with hard structural guards; conversely, purely structural allocation (equalized-random turns) demonstrably breaks adjacency pairs, and the semantic echo class (mutual-confirmation spirals) is invisible to string/ID-level machinery ŌĆö only discipline catches it. The protocol floor is therefore designed as *"a bottom that keeps an ill-disciplined participant from breaking the room"*, not as a scheduler that speaks for well-behaved ones.

#### 13.30.2 The room object
A board MAY host any number of rooms. `{ roomId, topic, mode: 'persistent'|'temporary', moderated: bool, participants: [{ agentId, role: 'moderator'|'participant'|'observer', voice: bool, speakerClass: 'human-operator'|'agent' }], floor: { holder?, queue[] }, budgets: { maxConsecutive, ratePerMin, maxAutoHop, stallRounds }, artifacts: { header, decisions[], summary }, createdBy, createdAt, closedAt? }`. A `temporary` room dissolves on explicit close or when its purpose is declared met (MUC-lineage `temporary` semantics); `persistent` rooms survive restarts. `role` is session-scoped standing *in this room*; it is deliberately distinct from board-level standing (the MUC role-vs-affiliation split).

#### 13.30.3 Envelope extensions
A room message is a normal CUSTOM envelope (msgId, ack tiers, dedup ŌĆö all ┬¦13.13 machinery inherited) plus: **`roomId`** ┬Ę **`addressee[]`** (explicit naming ŌĆö marks a response *obligation* on the named participants; the adjacency-pair anchor) ┬Ę **`replyTo`** (msgId of the first pair part being answered) ┬Ę **`floorIntent`** (`request` | `release` | `yield`, optionally with a scalar importance bid) ┬Ę **`authority`** (`directive` | `proposal` | `info` ŌĆö an agent-authored instruction-shaped utterance is demoted to `proposal` by default; promotion to binding requires a human ack or a pre-delegated scope) ┬Ę **`notice`** (bool ŌĆö "automated output, MUST NOT be auto-replied to"; the Matrix `m.notice` rule as a message class; watcher guidance: the recommended default is **non-wake** for turn-based participants unless the receiver is in `addressee[]` ŌĆö keeps room traffic aligned with the ┬¦13.16.9 wake economy) ┬Ę **`autoHop`** (server-maintained depth of the agent-reply chain since the last human utterance).

#### 13.30.4 Server-enforced floor (deterministic bottom)
1. **Fan-out** ŌĆö a room message is relayed to every participant over the existing 1:1 targeted path (at-least-once + commitment ack inherited unchanged). *Announce once, reach all.* Turn-spawned local workers (a supervisor that spawns a model turn per inbound ŌĆö ┬¦13.27 lineage) MUST NOT treat every fan-out copy as a wake trigger: wake only on delegation-class work or when named in `addressee[]`, cursor-advance otherwise (first-day dogfood: a scribe worker woke once per room utterance and spent whole turns reporting "not applicable").
2. **autoHop cap** ŌĆö when `autoHop Ōēź budgets.maxAutoHop`, further agent replies in that chain are **parked** and a `RoomStall` event is emitted. Never a silent drop: silence-by-fallback is the documented failure smell of LLM speaker selection. The default cap sits **above** the conduct layer's self-cap (D4: 3-5) with margin ŌĆö default `maxAutoHop: 6` ŌĆö so a discipline-compliant participant never hits the floor first (the floor is a bottom for the ill-disciplined, not a ceiling on the compliant). Parking is record-only, no auto-release: the resume path is a human/moderator utterance resetting the chain, after which the parked sender MAY re-send ŌĆö re-gated through D1 (only if the message is still worth saying).
3. **Rate + consecutive caps** ŌĆö per-agent per-room rate limit, and a cap on consecutive utterances by the same speaker (the generalization of `allow_repeat_speaker`).
4. **Stall detection** ŌĆö N rounds with no new addressee and no new decision ŌåÆ `RoomStall` ŌåÆ escalate to the moderator (if any) or the human.
5. **Human priority** ŌĆö a `human-operator` utterance broadcasts a **soft-yield** event: agents finish the turn in flight, then MUST incorporate the human utterance before starting a new one (the text-domain form of barge-in-yields). Humans are exempt from rate/voice constraints.
6. **Floor state single source of truth** ŌĆö the server owns `floor` (BFCP lineage). In v1 it is *advisory*: naming and self-selection discipline drive who speaks; the server only tie-breaks concurrent `floorIntent: request` bids and guards against starvation. Hard floor assignment is deliberately NOT in v1.
7. **Notice-class surfacing** ŌĆö an agent auto-reply to a `notice` message is surfaced as a warning event (visible discipline violation), not blocked.

#### 13.30.5 Room artifacts (shared context beyond the log)
Three pinned artifacts, per the ledger/blackboard lineage: **header** (room objective + currently-valid plan + role boundaries + **per-participant expected-latency declarations** ŌĆö e.g. `latency: turn-based ~50min` ŌĆö so a turn-based peer's pace is a declared property, not a discipline violation; versioned ŌĆö a change emits an invalidation event, not a re-broadcast of the full text) ┬Ę **`decisions[]`** (append-only with `supersedes` links; "currently valid" is always HEAD) ┬Ę **`summary`** (running digest with an explicit `covers_until` message cursor ŌĆö before the cursor the digest speaks, after it the raw tail does; re-based from the raw log periodically to cap summary drift). A room announcement replaces N 1:1 deliveries only when all four hold: the content is a **single canonical artifact with a version id**; recipients have a **consumption duty** (turn-start probe); confirmation is **ack-by-reference** (quoting the version id, unconfirmed recipients tracked); changes propagate as **invalidation + delta**. Individual delegations still restate a one-line anchor plus the pointer (the deliberate-redundancy safety net). Artifact fetch contract: `RequestRoomArtifacts { roomId }` ŌåÆ `RoomArtifacts { roomId, artifacts, version }` reply, plus the same event broadcast on change (invalidation + delta) ŌĆö WS-only, symmetric with `RequestChannelHistory`. The write path is `RoomArtifactsUpdate { roomId, header? {text}, decision? {text, supersedes?}, summary? {text, covers_until} }` ŌĆö participants and the board only; the server stamps editor/timestamp/per-artifact versions, appends decisions (`rd-<n>`, never rewritten), and broadcasts the delta under a single monotonically increasing artifacts `version` (the ack-by-reference target). Digest upkeep is naturally a scribe-worker duty (┬¦13.23): the room owner delegates a summary refresh, the scribe reads the room channel tail and submits `RoomArtifactsUpdate { summary }` with an honest `covers_until` cursor.

#### 13.30.6 Conduct discipline (the agent-owned layer)
Normative procedure lives in the **`/roundtable` skill** (constellation plugin); the protocol only summarizes the nine duties so adopters know what the floor assumes: ŌæĀ silence is the default output (respond-or-not is a separate decision made *before* content generation) ŌæĪ being named in `addressee[]` creates a response obligation ŌĆö answer or explicitly yield Ōæó unsolicited speech goes through `floorIntent: request` with an honest importance bid ŌæŻ agentŌåöagent exchanges self-cap (3-5 turns) without human input, then pause with a one-line state summary Ōæż late joiners and turn-based participants re-hydrate in fixed order ŌĆö header ŌåÆ valid decisions ŌåÆ summary ŌåÆ raw tail after `covers_until`; never a full replay Ōæź announcements are consumed via ack-by-reference Ōæ” closing is a structured field, not a magic string Ōæ¦ a human utterance is a soft-yield event Ōæ© the moderator hat, when assigned, holds procedure authority only (agenda, timebox, periodic summarization, participation management, decision capture) ŌĆö never content authority.
