Wake-path note (dogfooded): a turn-based participant SHOULD dual-path its wake source ŌĆö a short-interval poll watcher plus an independent long-period fallback. A single pipeline watcher is one buffering bug away from silent deafness: in the first room dogfood, a mid-pipeline filter stage without per-line flushing trapped events in a 4 KiB block buffer, and the room looked idle to that participant while traffic flowed.

#### 13.30.7 Vocabulary & compatibility
Naming is deliberately aligned to the MUC/Matrix lineage ŌĆö `voice`, `moderated`, `moderator`, `notice`, `temporary` ŌĆö because the concept vocabulary is the longest-lived layer of this section. A2A compatibility guard: the room correlation key is an opaque string, never coupled 1:1 to an A2A `contextId` (a room may span many); room participation remains expressible as "N 1:1 sessions + server fan-out", so if the A2A ecosystem later standardizes a group extension, a room server becomes its host rather than its competitor.

#### 13.30.8 Dashboard projection
The prompt-target selector (┬¦13.23.4) gains a **"Ō×Ģ roundtable"** entry: topic input + multi-select of targets (group toggles included) + persistent/temporary choice ŌåÆ creates the room and a tab under a **roundtable tab group** (lazy-materialized like all A2A tabs). The tab renders the conversation plus collapsible pinned header/digest and participant chips (­¤Äż voice ┬Ę ­¤¬ä moderator ┬Ę ­¤æż human). It is a *sending* surface (input enabled, target = the room), unlike read-only monitors. Room utterances are excluded from echo-mode (┬¦13.26) mirroring ŌĆö an agent's contribution to a room goes through the D1 gate only, never as an automatic mirror.

### 13.31 Board state schema ŌĆö the data contract behind the dashboard

#### 13.31.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.57 (2026-07-18). The live-board state document has driven the dashboard since the board's first cut, but its field contract existed only as renderer code. An adopter measured the cost: a stage list written as `{name, state}` against the renderer's `{label, status}` contract survived two hygiene sweeps while rendering every stage as pending ŌĆö render fallbacks silently swallow near-miss schemas (the consumer-contract lesson; see the boardsweep skill's schema-normalization clause). A second field observation: agents across adopting projects barely used the stage timeline at all ŌĆö the feature was undiscoverable (absent from worker charters and from any spec surface) and the incentive misaligned (mid-work updates read as pure cost). This section makes the contract canonical and pairs it with a usage discipline.

#### 13.31.2 The state document
Top-level keys of the board state document (server-watched, live-rebroadcast on change): `projects[]` `{id, name, color}` ŌĆö the group registry every entry's `project` references ┬Ę `modes` (board-scoped operating policy: language, tone, pace, routing) ┬Ę `freeRequest` (standing operator request) ┬Ę `current[]` ┬Ę `done[]` (newest-first) ┬Ę `planned[]` ┬Ę `decisions[]`. Common entry fields: `id` (the idempotency key for worker-applied updates ŌĆö REQUIRED on anything a delegation may touch twice) ┬Ę `project` (Ōłł `projects[].id`) ┬Ę `title` (REQUIRED) ┬Ę `when` (date) / `at` (ISO timestamp) ┬Ę `detail` ┬Ę `commit` / `ref` (VCS anchors ŌĆö the retrospective sweep verifies them against the repository). `planned[]` adds: `priority` (ascending sort, absent = lowest) ┬Ę `blocked` + `blockReason` + `unblock` ┬Ę `waiting` (autonomous wait vs actionable now). `decisions[]` adds: `status` (`'open'` | `'resolved'`) ┬Ę `kind` ┬Ę `question` ┬Ę `options[]` ┬Ę `recommend` ┬Ę `reviewedText` + `reviewedAt` (the resolution record; `detail` is plain text with `\n` line breaks, rendered escaped).

#### 13.31.3 Stage timelines (`current[]`)
A `current[]` entry MAY carry a staged progress shape: `stages: [{ label, status: 'pending' | 'active' | 'done' }]` ŌĆö exactly these key names and status values. The renderer treats any unknown status as `pending`: fallback-not-error is deliberate forward compatibility, but it is also precisely why near-miss schemas fail silently ŌĆö validate against **this** contract, not against plausibility. Optional companions: `sub[]` (sub-items, each MAY carry its own mini `stages`) and `blockedBy` (a `sub` index or a sub `id`; when it matches an existing sub-item the renderer draws the blocker link, and dangling references are ignored). The `active` stage's label doubles as the entry's one-line progress summary.

#### 13.31.4 Usage discipline
The schema only pays when entries actually use it: ŌæĀ a multi-stage track (roughly 3+ distinguishable phases, or work spanning sessions or external waits) SHOULD be registered on `current[]` **with** `stages` at start ŌĆö the scheduling round's "start it now" step is the natural hook; ŌæĪ status transitions happen at stage boundaries only (entering or finishing a phase), never per-action ŌĆö keeping the update cost near zero is what makes the discipline sustainable; Ōæó on completion the entry moves to `done[]`, where the `commit`/`ref` anchor is the durable evidence (carrying the final stage list is optional); ŌæŻ worker charters that apply board updates MUST carry this schema ŌĆö `stages` included ŌĆö so delegations can express it; a charter without the field is exactly how the contract stayed undiscoverable; Ōæż the retrospective sweep checks `stages` claims like any other board claim ŌĆö an `active` stage on an abandoned track is drift; Ōæź **sweep cadence** ŌĆö the retrospective pass runs **work-denominated, not wall-clock** (drift accumulates with off-board work, not with time): (a) **at session resume** ŌĆö after a context compaction or workspace restart, before new board-relevant work; the post-compaction window is the highest-misregistration window on record (a measured resume-time sweep surfaced 12 record corrections, including identifier ghosts that had survived 40+ cuts), and quick scope (recent `done[]` + everything open on `current`/`planned`/`decisions`) suffices unless it surfaces anomalies; (b) **every ~5 release cuts or 7 days, whichever comes first** ŌĆö full scope, resolving every recorded identifier against the repository; only the full pass catches slow corruption (lost tags, rewritten-away commits); (c) **on the idle signature** (resident boards ŌĆö headless hub-mains, peer-run boards): board-update traffic silent for a window (suggest 24h) *while* work signals (commits, A2A traffic) continue ŌĆö silence plus ongoing work is the drift signature, silence with no work needs no sweep; the ┬¦13.27 loop's idle tick is the natural executor; (d) **immediately after history-shape operations** ŌĆö tag moves, history rewrites, force pushes ŌĆö the class that mints unresolvable identifiers.

#### 13.31.5 Cross-links
┬¦13.16.6 (watcher/cycle discipline the scheduling round composes with) ┬Ę ┬¦13.20 (blocker manifest ŌĆö `blockedBy` is its `current[]`-local cousin) ┬Ę ┬¦13.23 (board-worker projection ŌĆö the charter is the enforcement point) ┬Ę the boardsweep skill (consumer-contract normalization) and the roundnext skill (start-with-stages hook).

### 13.32 Onboarding flows ŌĆö direct-server vs peer-join, ports, loopback-first

#### 13.32.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.70 (2026-07-19). Second spec cut of the gateway-status program (the harness-adapter contract's candidate maps are the first). Constellation onboarding has so far been learned by imitation of the reference deployment; this section makes the entry decision explicit so setup tooling and candidate-host guides (resident gateways as hub-mains, messaging daemons as local workers) share one flow.

#### 13.32.2 The two entry paths
Every onboarding starts with one decision ŌĆö **who owns the board?**

- **Direct-server operation** ŌĆö the project hosts its own board: server + dashboard + a main-agent bridge (`WS_PRIMARY_AGENT` set at spawn, ┬¦13.1). Choose this when the joining agent *is* the project's main (a new project standing up its coordination surface; a resident gateway serving as hub-main per ┬¦13.9.3 with per-boundary profiles). The reference self-board deployment is the template: start script owns server + dashboard sync + worker supervisor as one unit.
- **Peer join** ŌĆö the board already exists and the agent attaches to it: as **peer-main** (`peer` kind, ┬¦13.16.11 ŌĆö another project's main), as a **local worker** (local key + charter, ┬¦13.23), or as a **collab agent** (collab key, ┬¦13.9). Choose this when the project surface belongs to someone else; the joiner's duty profile (┬¦13.9.3) ŌĆö not its wire role ŌĆö decides what it does after the handshake.

The rubric is ownership, not capability: an agent capable of hosting still joins as peer when the project surface is not its own (one project = one board; two mains on one board is the ┬¦13.25.7 multi-hat confusion this split exists to prevent).

#### 13.32.3 Port assignment (single device, multiple boards)
Multiple boards on one device collide on fixed default ports ŌĆö resident daemons in the candidate-host class all bind fixed defaults, and the reference dual topology (hub on one port, self-board on another) is itself a manual instance of the rule that follows. The onboarding contract for setup tooling: **auto conflict-avoidance by default, manual pin as the advanced path.** Default flow ŌĆö probe the preferred port; on conflict, scan upward deterministically; **record the chosen port in the deployment config** so the assignment is stable across restarts (an unrecorded auto-port is a drift generator: every restart may re-roll it and strand bridges). Manual pin remains first-class for operators running reverse proxies or multi-device topologies. The reference runtime accepts an explicit port at spawn; the auto-avoidance flow is a contract on *tooling*, not a claim that the current server self-scans.

#### 13.32.4 Security ordering (loopback-first)
Onboarding order is part of the security model: the board comes up **loopback-only first** (┬¦13.25 secure-by-default bind), and exposure beyond loopback happens only *after* the access controls it depends on are configured ŌĆö keys required on the agent surface, allowlists on UI/MCP, then the explicit expose opt-in (┬¦13.25's toggle + restart path). Publicly documented incident classes of internet-exposed agent gateways (unauthenticated daemons discovered at internet scale, remote-compromise CVEs) are the standing justification: the failure mode is not exotic, it is *default-on exposure*. Remote access for distributed teams routes through a private overlay network or an authenticating proxy rather than a raw public bind. Setup tooling and onboarding guides MUST present exposure as a separate, later step ŌĆö never as part of first-run.

#### 13.32.5 Cross-links
┬¦13.1 (roles at HELLO) ┬Ę ┬¦13.9.3/┬¦13.9.4 (duty profiles, ephemeral peers) ┬Ę ┬¦13.16.11 (key kinds) ┬Ę ┬¦13.23 (worker projection) ┬Ę ┬¦13.25 (access control mechanism ŌĆö this section is its *ordering*) ┬Ę `plugins/HARNESS-ADAPTER-CONTRACT.md` ┬¦7-┬¦8 (candidate hosts whose onboarding these flows serve) ┬Ę `constellation/BOOTSTRAP.md` (the start-to-finish operational guide that walks these flows end to end).
